O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the culmination of the knowledge of medicine along with its practice, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is lost in our region and has become foreign to everyone, thus the knowledge has perished and disappeared, and there remains nothing of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this come errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is made distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 Or it seems to me that I want to bring this treatise to life according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I will also discuss the forms of the irons for cauterization and other tools used in the work with the adjustment of the declaration and their preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And because in our time no good master of hands can be found, the art of medicine is abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to be knowledgeable in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of them, and their movement and resting, and the place from which they issue. ‌
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And because Ipocras said that the name with the name is much, and with the work it is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	 and likewise in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that if one is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, he should guard himself against falling into error and harming men;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 just as I have seen many times with those who dabble in this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 For I saw a foolish physician who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 causing so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another physician who extracted a stone from a man's eye, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 and carried away with it a piece of the eyeball, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one cut him, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another physician who undertook to treat a Duke of our land whose leg was broken, and with the fracture he had an open wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the physician, full of ignorance, pulled on the fracture over the wound with forceps, and left no salve at all on the wound, and left it thus for one term.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 And he ordered him not to dislocate it at all.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And so it remained until the leg was completely swollen and the foot became gangrenous.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I was called to come to him and hurried to come and dislocate the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 And when I heard it had been dislocated, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But nevertheless, the corruption had already taken hold in the limb, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 And the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the whole limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another physician who opened an encysted abscess and then inflamed it through the malevolence of his practice.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corruption can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 That is to say, works where there is danger in many ways; abei li oevres que nus ne pued faire sanz peril. Et por ceu est li mestiers asses prou et difficiles.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 Therefore, you must be careful so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 So take up your arms in confidence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you may come to safety and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And leave the dreadful diseases to those who have great knowledge.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may pass from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Ne take not in charge bad illness, lest you be called foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and also about medical cautery, and this chapter is organized from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 And of the shapes of the instruments, and of the tools for cauterization, and of all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 The second chapter is also about cutting and boring, and about cupping and wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 And this chapter is organized according to the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 and is ordered from the head to the feet, and of the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 As we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak about the quality of each temperament and its harmfulness.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest speech and most subtle knowledge and secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 and many wise men have spoken of this and agreed upon it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 but I am not satisfied with their words, for I fear verbosity.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that cautery helps universally in all complexions where there is material, except for two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 that is to say, hot complexion without material and dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In hot and dry complexions together with material, some have discussed and said that cautery is great help there;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 And others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 That cautery is not good for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured with heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 And those who say the opposite claim that cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that occur in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 Because when you examine the man's body and its moisture according to the fire complexion, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 Because I have found it so by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 And yet, do not interfere with it except for those who have experienced it, and who know through long practice the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and duration of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not extend beyond the member that it burns, and does no harm to any other member if possible.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 The burning medicines come from one member to another, spreading, and cause disease with serious healing in the affected member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 And by chance kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire, because of its high intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 And this I have found through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, and it was based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 And for this reason I apologize for the length of my speech, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosophers say, demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 Or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed upon the time when the cauteries should be made, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harm that occurs is remedied by the aid of cauterization.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And also if the cauterization is necessary for urgent and pressing pains, which cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 And do not think of it, dear son, as foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 for the disease that is healed by cauterization does not recur;
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say it thus; 》
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is nothing more than a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and it is more effective than other medicines due to its quick action, and the power of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And it is possible for the illness to come sometimes according to the constitution of the patient and the location of the illness and its power;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 and the superfluous elements are gathered in him by the consumption of food and similar things, except for cauteries applied to a place where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as tooth cauterization for pain, and similar things, and this kind of pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	 but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 but they do not believe that cautery is worthwhile after medicine, but their belief is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer remedies in some illness and they are not effective, then we apply the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and they said that cauteries of gold are more effective than those of iron, as they have declared.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	 They do at the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 Now I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that it may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and it has two effects: it is done because of an illness called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, due to excessive dreams and toothache and throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine, changing the head (i.e., making it wet) for III or IV nights, according to what the virtue and nature and custom of the patient can bear;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 then make the head of the patient dry again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 Then have him sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands on a soft cushion;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 after that, place the root of your palm at the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 and where your two fingers meet, make it bleed first. Then warm the cautery called "olive," for this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And put it on the spot with a stamped ink mark, and make as you descend and press your hand little by little in turn.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 then immediately lift your hand, and return to the spot if you see a bone appear a little.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 and if you do not see it, then begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 afterwards take a small amount of silk, and put inside it soft cotton, and place on the spot, and leave it there for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 afterwards place a moistened cloth with butter on top.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 and leave it in place until the burn has healed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And the ancients said that the longer an open wound remains, the more it purges itself.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and for this reason, it needs to be moved around.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some said that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what is burnt from the bone, and it should be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that one should leave the cautery on for so long, and press it so hard that you remove the bone as wide as a spindle that women use for spinning, so that the humors may flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterwards, it should be cleaned and sewn up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 And these two methods of cauterization do not seem entirely good to me, except in some men where there is reason for fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and I think that I should leave it; xspace 127
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 and likewise when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and healthier to me, then I work on that together with healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts for a long time, then the patient should use irises and pills that are called "cock's comb", and of purging of the head and of oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 and if one performs the cautery that we have spoken of before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Take care that the patient's head is not of a strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize under that cautery a little bit, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 After that, make a cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place called "vessel".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 And it is the place where one puts cupping glasses.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 And lift your hand so that you do not see the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 The patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it elsewhere.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 And the cauteries of the horns should be more subtle than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the method.
dou cautere dou chief	 of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the eye is purged with cleansing medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and none of these help.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 Then he makes cauterizations according to two methods, namely with hot iron and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 The cauterization with hot iron is done by taking a piece of alder wood, removing the bark and chopping it into two pieces, then making an incision in the place where the pain is felt so that you can insert the piece of alder wood under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 and when it has been inserted, tie it and press it firmly, leaving it in place for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 and then untie it and pull it out, and leave the wound open for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 then place a cotton ball soaked in butter on it until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the wound has healed from the ointment treatment;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 And if you see it done thus, do as with some burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth chapter about burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery whose shape is as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 And it is called "clo" because the head is made in the shape of a nail with a hollow at its tip, and in the middle it has a small opening.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 And place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand steady and turn it a little lightly, so that half of its thickness is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And lift your hand so that the part outside does not burn, and there will be an abundance of blood flowing out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Afterwards, place cotton wool in vinegar, and put it on the spot for three days.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then put moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cautellare", then do so at the very tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	 of a migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When you cure this migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the previous cautery of medicine and iron does not help him at all, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 And thus on the painful place a line of half two units long, and remove your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cut the artery and do not go as far as the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 And beware of the jaw that moves when one eats, and the nerve should not have regard for it or spasm come to the patient, and beware of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where there is great fear in cutting, and also for him who does not know about it, who is not learned and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 And leave the work halfway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 But I will tell you how to staunch blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it is needed in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 And if you see, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, along with the cautery that has two knives.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the ear pain due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from cold, and one has worked with solvent medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 After pointing all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and you move away a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 And it should have ten points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 Of the mouth's torment
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 Ailment that must be cured by cautery is none other than those that originate from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And not to make a cautery on similar things that come from dryness and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When you treat this similar condition of pain that comes from the flux of humors and purges of the head and gargles, and it does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 one on the root of the ear, and another a little below the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 and place the cautery in the healthy part of the body, and give a cautery on the top of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 and let the cautery remain until half of the hair is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And it resembles the knife that we mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and the knife should be a little larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after curing the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 When the stroke is old and you treat it as we have said, and there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place that is called «vasselz» as we have said before, and the last cautery on the stomach's opening.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	 of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 For this illness, one should give the patient large doses and pills that modify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 then wash the head of the patient thoroughly, and apply a mustard plaster to the occiput, as written in the section on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 and this is the manner of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If he is cured in this way, good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 and if he is not, then let him undergo three cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, with two fingers' width between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	 and treat him as the others, and if you see it worsening, and the patient is tolerant, let him undergo one cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if necessary, two more on the two horns, and continue the treatment until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 And let the cautery be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hair and of what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 after shaving the head of the patient, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the disease is strong, make four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	 and leave it until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 After the treatment, until he is healed, and let the cautery called "olivare" which we have previously mentioned be done.
de l’epilempsie	 Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use the cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make him a gargle and chew, softening the brain often with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 After washing his head in the middle, and there make a cautery according to what we have said before, and make a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if the patient is strong and tolerant, make him a cautery as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olivier according to the method that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are corrupt and excessive humours or thick phlegm, then use the cautery of thin needles as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if the superfluidity inclines towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as was previously explained in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After washing the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 then make a bandage of linen well made, like a circle, and place it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 and let the patient sit with their arms crossed, and be held firmly from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 then present the linen cloth, and anoint it well with old sheep butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 and heat it over a moderate fire, so that one can touch it without being burned;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 then place the circle inside on the head, and let it cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and do this for the patient once each week with other good treatment until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 And if you see cauterizing the wound by making several points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of cauterization moistens the brain equally well;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 And then place moistened cotton soaked in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the movement of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When the movement first comes to the eyes by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to cleanse the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 Then instruct the patient to lean their head back, and perform a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on each of the temples if the flow is into both eyes at once, or one if the flow is into one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 and cut off all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 and beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then staunch it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	 And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incisions how to staunch it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And sometimes one performs cautery or branding under the two bones behind
dou cors des larmes	 du corps des larmes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When tears of the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the head outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	 and one sees that it is from cold phlegmatic excesses, then make the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of the eye, descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	 perform cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries with the brand under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 And if more is needed, then cauterize it wisely on top of the skull with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 Of the body tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	 When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit at all, then give the patient three nights of cold drinks;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	 after the king of the head, and makes a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	 and makes two cauteries of the type called "nail" on the two shoulders, one a little below the armpits
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the papilla of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	 de la raison pourquoi cela se produit :
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	 And if you see [it] this way, make two cauteries on the two shoulders as long as the shoulders are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 and do not leave [the fire] there except until the third part of the skin is burnt, according to the method that I have said
dou poil qui point l’oil	 of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes turns backwards and pricks the eye, and then one makes cauteries in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 This means "it is to know about fire, or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 Instruct the patient that they should let their hair grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 And if they prick at their base, he should hold his eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow out.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in your hand;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 Next, trace on the skin of the eyes a shape that is like the leaves of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then place moistened cotton in egg white and musk on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 Après cautériser sur le visage où tu as placé un peu de poche, fait-le plusieurs fois afin que l'endroit soit brûlé.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 And the sign of the healthiness of the work is that you see the skin shrink and the hairs raised to the point of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 Then raise your hand and leave it like this for three days, then apply cotton soaked in butter until the burn is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the cure of ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And if after this the hairs come back and the skin is softened, then repeat the cautery in the same place, as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a form from parchment like the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 Then take one .З. of French soap and one .З. of quicklime, grind them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 and make it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid paper.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 And if the patient is affected in only one eye, one should work on that one, and if in both eyes as well.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 And place moistened cotton beneath the eye in vinegar.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 And let the head of the patient be in your hand and place your finger on top of the ointment, and press the pouch and move it each time the patient feels the burning of the ointment, for they feel the burning as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for some time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the burning has passed, lift up the skin, and look if you see the flesh raised as if it were lifted by the constriction of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 and if so, then all is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If not, then apply more ointment to the place where the ointment has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are focused;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then place a piece of cloth soaked in butter over the burned area until the heat subsides, then treat the ointment area, which is called "diaphenes" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you must watch carefully your work with great care lest any of the medicine fall into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin the treatment again on the area that has been softened by the skin properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the healing of the treatment until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 and the right way should not be denied to those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you burn it with a cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Command the patient to place his head in your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 and let the servant hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor should he lower his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 After, place moistened cotton in egg white or parsley juice over the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 After, heat the iron which is thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 And it is shaped at the tip like the quill of a feather, together with the nail being the cauterizing iron.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent pole.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 However, this shaped one is more suitable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After, press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 And if it is closed, then open it, and draw out the head.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 After, place the hot iron strongly on [the wound], and hold your hand on the iron at the side of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not slip.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 And place the cautery in the oil’s fat, and it corrupts.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you approach the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If not, then reapply the cautery once more, or again if needed, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 afterwards place a moistened cotton ball in butter, and use the dry dressing until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, apply a corrosive medication until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 And the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a manner of cautery for fistulas that some ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 Understand a fistula, and open the site;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Afterward, place in the opening one subtle camphanum of this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and it is made to the amount of one-third of an ounce of lead;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 And hold your hand firmly on the cauterizing iron, and let the patient not move at all, lest the molten lead run to his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 And it is necessary that one place on the patient's eye moistened cotton in white of egg or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 The lead is also useful for the place of a fistula, and the healthy one by marvelous healthiness.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then a perforation must be made in the nostril, and the fistula should be brought back to the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Mouth ulcers often occur on the lips called "hair", and similarly on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these ulcers as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then heat a small cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 And put it quickly in those cracks until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the place with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the throat abscess
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or the eye, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and afterward it becomes putrid and rotten and is swollen and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 And you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not benefit at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 Therefore, it is necessary for you to have the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 after the hole or opening of the fistula, and keep your hand so that the iron comes to the bottom of it, and in the lower place;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this once or twice, after the treatment that we have said in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of the teeth's movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the patient in your hand;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 After heating the cautery, which will be described hereafter, place a reed over the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 And quickly insert the hot cautery into it, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 Afterwards, remove your hand and restart the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 Then let the patient rinse his mouth with salt water, holding it in for an hour and spitting it out forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture causing corruption is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	 of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 When toothache comes from cold, whether it is in the air or wind, and medical treatments do not work, then there are two methods of cautery needed.
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 And that of butter and that of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 Cautery with butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and put the end in an iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent peg, and moisten it in melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 and thus do often until its power comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see so moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on it until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a reed of iron or bronze, and it should be thick enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 après que tu as chauffé le cautère (de sorte que sa forme vienne comme indiqué ci-dessus), place-le sur la dent et maintiens ta main en place jusqu'à ce que le cautère soit refroidi.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 fais ceci souvent, car la douleur disparaîtra le même jour ou le lendemain.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 Et il faut que le patient remplisse sa bouche de bon beurre avant l'application du cautère, puis qu'il rince sa bouche.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 et voici la forme du cautère :
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 Et fais un cautère sur n'importe quelle dent que tu veux, en fonction de tes capacités.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 et voici la forme de la canne :
des scrophules	 of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 Lorsque les scrophules sont causées par des humeurs froides et humides, et qu'elles ne répondent pas à la digestion par des médicaments, alors chauffe le cautère comme indiqué ci-dessous. Il doit avoir deux ouvertures pour permettre aux fumées de s'échapper du côté opposé du cautère.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 And place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it there for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 And place a cotton swab moistened with butter over the burn until the blister is removed.
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterward, treat the area with onions and linseed until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When moisture prevails on the channels of the brain, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be emptied by purgative medicines.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 Afterwards, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go as far as the throat, but only a little way into the esophagus.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 After that, he makes another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle" as we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When the disease is due to cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the disease is chronic, he should make two cauteries on the temple in close places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form that was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking into the entirety of the cautery that is called "finger" as its form is described here in the case of ear disease;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And let the points go as far as 30, or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the place according to what was said before, and let the cautery be at three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because the cauteries are lighter, therefore you make three in succession.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Afterwards, have the patient lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 afterwards lift the heart which is inside the ribcage with your left hand's two fingers;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has 2 nerves below it, as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the side, and let the shape of the cautery be accompanied by 4 other cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 and for this reason, make a cautery with the 3-nerve cautery, so that the figure of the cauterization is made up of these 6 cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the 3-nerve cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, so that there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 After place the cautery made of burnt hemp seed;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 then make the patient rest, and do not move the member for a long time until it is well rested.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, which happens rarely, then make a cautery above the thick part of the burn, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and much moisture come into the stomach to such an extent that it strains his complexion, and many catarrhs befall him, and in the usual ways of treatment he does not benefit, then the patient must be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 Then afterwards make three cauteries: one below the heel of the foot by the width of a finger, with all the cautery blazing, and two cauteries on either side so that the shape of the cauteries is in three corners, and there is such space between them that they do not touch each other when they emit pus;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 and let the cautery be so deep that it reaches the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 Et si vous voyez cautériser avec un grand cautère dans l'estomac selon cette forme ;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 et celui qui aura peur de ce cautère, cautérisez en piquant et en touchant l'estomac à ce point selon la quantité que vous voyez d'en haut ;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 ensuite, faites céder tout le pus qui est appelé « poin ».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, until it heals.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 Lorsque le foie a de la douleur due au froid, à l'humidité et à une grande flatulence, cela signifie qu'il a été fortement altéré par des excès de substances ;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 et le patient n'est pas guéri par les moyens que nous avons mentionnés précédemment, et cela ne lui apporte aucun bénéfice, alors il faut qu'il soit traité sur la base de ses propres caractéristiques ;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 And make a sign of three cauteries according to this form and this shape and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press too much with your hand on all the cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 And let only half of the cautery be burned, and let the patient stand on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 And if he cannot, then let him be lying down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms.
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 And if your intent is to, then cauterize these cauteries with the cautery knife, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all the heart, for you would dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And let it not reach the boiling point, for the heart is very sensitive there, and you should know this for certain.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not very strongly;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 And if it is in the membrane, then the patient feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And then, when this treatment should be carried out by the doctors, it is necessary for the patient to be seated upright on his bed;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then have the place where the abscess is hot and then heat the cautery that resembles a grape, for this is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 And cauterize with the cautery until the heart is burnt, and reach up to the spleen, so that the entire viscera are all outside.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the care according to the care of the excrement until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 and it is not fitting that of this cautery anyone should use except those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and through whom many of these diseases have been corrected at some point.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 The ancients said that one should make for pleurisy cauteries from the roots of Aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 And wet it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the part that is beneath the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 And two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind a little;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	 And one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the ribs of the chest opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders.
