Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	 When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are on top of the head of the shoulder, and no medical treatment benefits it, and you see the face of the patient redden, and he feels a throbbing in his forehead as if trembling;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 and the eyes are cloudy and moist so that the hair of the eyelids has fallen out, and the eyelids are heated and scalded by the burning of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	 And the ancients called it "treatment for bruising," and it is that you should instruct the patient who has this disease to let the hairs grow on his forehead. Then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	 And let one of the incisions be like this: two fingers' width across the forehead, running down to the nose, and the others, two fingers' width apart, above the ribs. Be careful not to cut the arteries that are on the sides, above the ribs.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	 Keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be three fingers' width wide.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And have ready a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping away the blood, then apply the pointed spoon in two parts as shown here.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	 From the incision by the temples down to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 And scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions, along with the soft tissue that lies on the bone. Then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spoon firmly.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 If you insert into the first incision the instrument called "scalpel," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, it is this form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the sharp side towards the flesh to the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle of the incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the heart, and then make another cut in the middle fissure until the other extremity.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	 And then drain the blood equally, and press the area where the blood was taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	 Then place in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and garlic, and ensure that any abscess does not develop there.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And on the third day, loosen the bandage, and apply a large poultice of hot water, then treat with ointment made from basil and rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 Of the moisture of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	 When a person has an acute catarrh, and you see the eyes dimmed and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burnt;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	 and the hair falls out, and there is sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 then know by these symptoms that those substances and this catarrh come from many veins, and the appropriate treatment for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you command the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on both temples.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	 And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	 and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during chewing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	 and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then remove between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen bandages there;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	 then place on it cloths soaked in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere:	 In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	 take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 and administer it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	 All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 or grain, or beast, or stone from a mine or similar thing like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	 or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 And things flowing like water and easily, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear, stone or other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	 If you see the stone, then let some drops of violet oil or sesame oil drip onto it, then bring about its extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	 and make him sneeze with pepper, and stop up his nostrils when he is about to sneeze, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	 and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	 Many times this cure succeeds;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 and if it does not succeed, bring about the extraction with fine tweezers, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	 If it succeeds with tweezers, that's good; xspace Car il n’i ad point de perill, et ne desnature pas li membre.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	 if not, then bring about the extraction with a subtle little instrument of small size
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	 and if it does not come out by that means, then make a tube of bronze and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal strongly, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	 then pull very hard, for very often it comes out as we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	 and if it does not come out in this manner, then take birdlime and put it into some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull hard.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	 And if it does not jump out of all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear before an abscess or spasm comes.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	 And the manner of the split is that you first bleed the patient from the temples, and draw blood according to the measure of his strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the fat or hanging place;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	 And let the cut be like a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck on it quickly to your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	 And if there is pus which is inside and it swells, then administer extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it cannot come out, then administer a fine thin sponge according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision in that abscess
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	 But do not make it when you think that the pus is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 Then strain it through fine sieves and in a press, as we have said, so that the extraction may be light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 When water falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to sneeze first with condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 if it jumps through this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	 And if not, then take many stones according to the length of your hand, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; xspace
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	 And put the patient on one side of his ear, and make him sit on his feet on the other side, and strike another stone against the stone that is in the ear;  xspace abei
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	 And do not stop making as if of stone on stone until all the water has come out, and so it jumps out all at once;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	 And if you see it, take a reed and put one end in the ear, and set fire to the other end until the reed is completely burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 Then do this again with other reeds until all the water has come out, as we have said before regarding stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	 In extracting a small creature, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the section on division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	 but if it is large enough to be felt, then use an extraction by puncture;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 And this is the easiest way to remove anything that might be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	 In the extraction of maggots from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section on distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear towards the sun.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 If there are any maggots present, draw them out with fine tweezers. And if they cannot be seen, then take the cane as we have described its form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	 And insert the finer end into the ear according to the amount of the patient's suffering. Then suck on it until the entire cane is empty.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Do this frequently until all the maggots come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	 And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop up around the cane with cotton as I have said in the previous section.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	 And if they do not protrude strongly as we have said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, then the form will be like this as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	 And whether it is made of silver or bronze, let there be small holes at the bottom and an opening above for distillation.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	 And to press in the distillation, use a well-made bronze instrument for this purpose. And if you wish, take a razor and wrap it tightly around the point with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	 Then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the reed, and let the reed be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	 Then put inside the ear all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is dripped into the opening of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	 and let the patient feel inside, and let the drops be heated in a pot over the fire before they are dripped into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 and ensure that it is not too cold, for then the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	 Some children are born with no opening in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	 and the same thing happens to adults due to the obstruction of a wound or born flesh inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes go very deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 and sometimes the pot pours out of the opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	 That which comes from the deepest part, if it cannot be seen, is of grave healing in many forms. And in that which can be seen, you must place the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	 and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 if you see the hairy part appear, then work with all this spatula of which there is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind fully, so that it does not wound the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 if the hair is of flesh or body of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers, and trim lightly until all that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the excision is deep in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	 If you feel the hair which causes the patient discomfort to hear, prick lightly and ensure that you do not damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 Then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisturize it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	 Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary to remove the tent and insert another tent moistened in ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling has subsided.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then continue the treatment until it is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding continues, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatise on distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of parchment
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	 This athelul that comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and scrape it off with a spatula made of its roots. 》
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 Then put on the place a preparation of vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	 And if it comes out, then cauterize with the subtle lens-shaped cautery, and afterwards the cauterizer should move around the incision.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	 and many times they return, until something remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 and when they are cauterized with fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	 of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	 Many times there come in the eyes something that seems like hail in its form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstone," and it is a mass of thick moisture in the eye, both above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	 the procedure is as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	 take care if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and this is a slight matter to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 make it wide, then lightly scrape each part, then take with tweezers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	 if you cannot cut without piercing the skin a little, it does not bother the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 and if the tear is large, stitch it together with one stitch, and treat until it is healed.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 and if it is small, do not use force, because the salve will restore it soon and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	 And if the earwax has descended into the ear toward the upper part, invert the skin, and extract the earwax with tweezers, and cut and press from one side and the other.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	 and if the skin is separated by the incision, it does not matter;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And when a carbuncle is cut, lift the eye with salt water, and treat the place of one who eats flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	 Exinach is a fat that is eaten on toasted bread, and this happens more often in children than in other people, and it afflicts their eyes greatly, and in the mornings they have catarrh, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 and therefore they always lie on their faces, and sleep face up, and their eyelids underneath are moist because the inflammation and appearance are covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you squeeze the place between your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	 And the manner of this work is such that the patient places his head in your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	 and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains externally each part, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	 and press with your two hands from both sides, so that the edges are gathered into the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	 then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit wide enough, and let it not be larger than the wound that is made for bleeding veins;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	 and pierce the skin completely until you reach the edges;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 and in many ways the edges of the slit come out, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	 Pull out then all at once a piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 And be careful not to approach the opening, so that you do not reach all the way to the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if the skin does not open at the beginning of the incision, gently widen the incision a little until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then pull it out as we have said, then moisten the cloth in oil and water, and place it on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then cure with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When hairs that are not natural appear on the eyelids and become entrenched, they harm the eyes and bring about various illnesses such as persistent tearing and softening of the lids and cornea, to the point that it causes blindness.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And there are four methods of treatment:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 either by cautery with fire, or by administering a drug according to what is said in the previous chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by canes, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 if it is inside out, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 if not, then you insert a needle with all of its thread above.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 and place it near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow, near these hairs, and draw the thread all the way along the eyelid, and turn it towards the nose.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 Then make an incision in the area under the skin, under the attached hairs, covering the entire surface, from the large lacrimal gland to the small one.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 Then pull the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the skin, then sew a figure on the skin, such as the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the skin which is divided for everyone.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And so, for someone who needs it, one should cut a large amount of skin according to how the skin is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 Then make an incision across the entire surface along the two lines you have marked, and begin from the large lacrimal gland down to the small one.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 and let one of them be a split near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the tip into one of the two corners of the heart, then peel it all off;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle with all one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluousness of the threads on the two edges stick to anything gluey, if you wish to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 and if not, then don't worry about it, but leave the stitch and the threads for three days or four;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 then cure the wound without stitches with dry and constricting things, for the skin heals by the healing of the wound and the assembling of it, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	 And there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 and it is that you trace the paper with a shape similar to the leaves of myrtle, as we have told you, three times devoided according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Then cut that which overhangs the small forces equally according to the form that is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and put it into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 and put another thread near the large tear duct, and a second thread near the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have traced, as we have told you, then join together the two lips of the wound with stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar ointments that ease.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 And sometimes it happens that the hair of the skin is turned:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 then you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 but the stitching in one and the other is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of dogs is according to this method:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 and it is that you turn the skin and the split inside as I have said, and then make two dogs by art, and two thin ligatures as long as the width of the spatula; 👉 And it is that you turn the skin and the split inside as I have said, and then make two dogs and two thin ligatures as long as the width of the spatula.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 And cut both heads of two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	 then assemble one with the other carefully on what hangs over the paper of the eye, and firmly hold the two handles of the two parts;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is held will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If it delays, then cut with force, then care for it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	 and when the wound has healed, and the paper has been lifted off, and the hairs will no longer grow.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 and this is the shape of the two handles that you will make according to this drawing, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	 The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put a thread of soft and fine silk through it.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	 Then join the heads [of the needle] and knot them together finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	 Then put another fine silk thread in the quiver [needle holder] briefly, and knot the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	 then have the patient place his head in your lap.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	 and let it be by the sunlight so that the work may be illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work. Then put the needle all the way into the quiver at the root of the hair, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you draw it over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	 Then pull out the hair until it reaches the flesh, and push into the flesh that hair, if there are one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 Then pull your hand until the hair comes out completely from all the flesh into the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	 And if the flesh is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then you will pull the flesh down to all the thread that you have ordered there, until the flesh comes out from the hole above and you see it with your eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	 Then pull out the flesh and the thread, and close the eye and the wound for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh rises.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is small, then accompany it with a long natural hair, and let it grow with that one until it is lengthened, and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the eye's infection
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or purulent matter comes into the eye, there are two kinds of it.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 One is natural, and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And the manner of treating it is to cut open that membrane, and separate its lips, and put inside linen threads, and leave it there until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And it is not necessary to use in the treatment of it things that dry out and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	 Because if you do this, then the disease returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	 But for softening agents, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 And let the rose of water or althea and flax seeds be cooked, and onions of the same type melted in some of the oils, and it is wrapped in a tent, and this is the cure for that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	 And the treasure of your treatment is to be careful that it does not close according to the shape it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 and this treatment that we have mentioned is not effective except as a remedy for this disease, so that it does not return to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness, which truly is called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	 The accident comes from a wound and from a cut and from cautery and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	 and the way to perform the treatment on it is that you take a needle with which there are two double threads, and the shaft in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left side of the cheek as far as the right, so that the thread comes out at two places in the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 Then the flesh should be raised above all the needle, and the cup should be wide like a spoon.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	 And if the appearance of the stone returns as it should, this is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	 If not, then take a scraper and place it in the cleft, and turn the stone, and make two clefts on either side within the stone;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	 And the heads of the two clefts should be at the two corners of the incision that you have scraped, and make such angles that when they are assembled, the appearance is like the letter which is called "Y.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	 Then remove that flesh according to the quantity whose sides are sharp beneath, following the stone, then join the two freed parts and sew them with a thread of wool.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, regarding the treatment of what we have said about softening medications and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	 And if the illness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make a clean cut under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	 Then, drain between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	 And one should perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine with all his might so that he may bring back the figure to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And the patient himself, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in many positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 from the joining of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	 When this suture happens to some men in such a way that the skin above is adhered with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must push the point of a razor under the skin, and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	 and use tweezers to cut it away, until you reach what is under the delicate membrane, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer from the membrane being too sharp and hurting the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	 and let your incision, with which you cut that assembly, be gentle, so that the skin returns to its natural shape.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	 and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes there is salty water in the eye, and lift it with fresh water, and with wine.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	 then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye abundant wool soaked in egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and after the third day use collyrium and other soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the fingernail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	 Know that the nail is according to two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	 it is nervous and similar to a hard cicatrix, and another which is not nervous but is similar to white frozen moisture, so that when one touches it with iron and tries to grab it with tongs, no one can.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 and both likenesses begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then closes his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	 and lifts the skin to your hand, then twists the nail in the tweezers with fine pliers, and extends it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	 then take a needle, and insert into it a hair of a horse or cow or ox, and make the thread strong;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	 and bend the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and push through to the end of the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upwards, and scrape off all the skin on the side of the nail that follows the vein and the silk along the hair until the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with all the subtle spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that through the incision does not come the body's usual tears.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	 And sometimes the nails extend to the nail bed, and to the thread, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 then after skinning, one has all the soft mucus from which this form is made;
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	 And ensure that the mucus does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the little plum is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And after the incision, throw into the eye a bit of boiled silk, and from the kohl made of lead oxide, and let it stay until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then the treatment of those who need it so that they may heal.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	 And if the nail is not fleshy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the instrument cannot enter, this appearance of a nail is often cured with medications.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see them covered, work with the eye of the patient, and take the fine spatula little sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And gently lift the nail above, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then drip from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of lead, red and burnt collyrium, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 then repeat the other work according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is wrong with the eye, such as an abscess, then leave it alone, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	 And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid night in the eye causing great harm, then suspend it with the hook, and cut part of it but not all, so that the body of tears does not come there;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 Then distill into the eye red choler made from lead.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 Of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	 In the eyes of some men there sometimes appears red flesh, and it covers the pupil and stretches onto the eyelids and turns outside, and it resembles a bawdy rose.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	 and the procedure is such that the patient places his head in your lap, then you open the eyes, and scrape all that flesh with appropriate tools for this purpose, and support it with strength.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	 then scrape the first layer of flesh, and continue scraping with the razor until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the procedure.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	 and let the incision of the spatula be such that we have described in the incision of the nail and small veins from which one removes the pus, as the form after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	 And when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, fill the wound with burnt oil in which you have distilled red-hot iron or similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton wool over it with a layer of egg white to ensure that the abscess is hot.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	 And if there is anything remaining, and the pus overcomes you, and you doubt that the abscess is hot, then leave the wound alone and treat the abscess with things that can soothe a hot abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 Then return to your work until it is healed, and do the same when flesh grows in the wound in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	 But nonetheless you must adapt the treatment for each weak wound according to its natural way.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	 And of the way of accident, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 And do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is able to endure the work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If they are red veins that cover the eye, and take away from sight its function and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	 Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which the arrow is lodged, is sound and there is no other disease besides the arrow.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	 Then take the eye in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins with all skill according to one's wisdom, and let the thread be fine and doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And let there be two ounces by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	 Then bind those veins firmly and tightly, and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see the veins retreat from the eye.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	 And be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut more than those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 And when you have done this, drop into the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the humour.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you cannot remove all of it in that hour, then make a plaster for the eye with soothing substances to relieve the pain, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and assured of heat from an abscess, then begin again according to this manner as before until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	 And this is the form of strength:
de la fistule de l’oil	 Of the anal fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	 The physician thus calls "healed" fissures:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 when you cure it by cautery and with hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is pus in it that you should incise over the abscess where it should die, and draw out all the moisture there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	 And when the bone is exposed and you see the putrefaction and blackness, then clean it with all the instruments whose form is described here.
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 and it is called "sharp hook," and should be made of iron, and should be pointed like a file as shown in the present form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	 And place under it the rotten bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the putrefaction is gone.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 and do this several times, then restore it with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 if the place is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the wound is healed, and it remains so for forty days, and does not reopen or become infected, and no bad accident happens, then know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	 if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the neck's opening according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 and it is that you uncover the bone for the second time with an iron instrument, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, then take a drill according to this form, and let the iron head be at three angles, and let the shaft be narrowed up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	 Then place it on the bone next to the eye socket, and move your hand away from the eye socket, then turn the whole auger until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels this because the air comes out if he keeps his hand on his nose.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	 And then restore the place with dry medicine, as I have shown you, and when the flesh heals and the place hardens, the matter goes to the nose.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 It is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	 When the eye is completely open and nothing interferes with the nose or makes it smaller, then you must tie up the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	 then heal it, then apply cupping glasses or cauterize without burning to draw out, then place on the eye a plaster made of alum and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then bandage the eye, and put a compress on top of bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	 and the manner of bandages is such that you take sufficiently soft bandages, and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	 then hold it firmly in place with a strong bandage, and reapply the cupping glasses to draw out without wounding;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	 then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye bandaged day and night, and if the bandage loosens, you must bandage it tightly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	 then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good;
se ce non;	 if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then reapply the poultice and the bandages and the bandage and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 Of the breaking of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	 Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, then it opens, and comes forth from the papers like a grain of resin, and is horrible to behold.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	 Then if you see it open, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper one, then thrust another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the arm.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	 and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to its position.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	 Then cut off the place of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around it, and hold it well, then withdraw the needle and place on top of the wound a wet linen cloth soaked in plenty of egg.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 And let it stay until the thread comes out with the pus, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And sometimes the wound is confined by a circle of cloth on every side until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	 And if the eye gives a great appearance of it, pierce it with a fine spatula that reaches to the bottom of the eye, and let the whitish moisture flow out, and immediately put something in.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	 This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but mucus that accumulates in the eye, resembling water descending, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	 And the manner of the appearance of the work is that you have the patient sit on a prepared and straight chair, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it until you see the vein coming above to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	 Then insert a needle, ensuring it does not descend and obscure the light, and let the patient see things as usual.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 And if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descent of the vein is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	 Then have the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and make an incision on the horny tissue at the junction with the horny layer and the corner of the eye, until the vein comes out.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when it comes out, drip hot water mixed with honey into the eye, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	 We have the likeness of waters in their nature, and those which must be pierced;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 do so according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and close the healthy eye and press very hard;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	 then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	 then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	 Then place the tip of the instrument next to the corona through the thickness of a ray in that part of the eye called the minor lacrimal gland, then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the eye's white, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	 And the measure of the path of almagda should be exactly equal to the measure of the space from the plumule up to the end of the pupil;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	 and this is the corona of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 then you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument where the water is, then press it along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if water flows now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	 After resting for a short time, and if the water rises again through the second passage, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, then gently pull out the amalgam while turning your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 And then put in a bit of fine salt, and remove from this the finger with the instrument.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place over the eye a compress or wet wool in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, use horseradish with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the almond cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	 And then pierce only the conjunctiva, do not go too deeply into it, but make a subtle place, then put in amalgam as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	 And at the completion of the work prepare a suitable bed for the patient, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	 And he should be free from all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him lie according to his condition until the third day.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	 then dislocate it in that same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 and it is not necessary to do this at the time of the treatment or after the incision now, but you must lift it up, because water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	 if swelling occurs, dislocate the eye before the seventh day and apply a poultice that relieves swelling;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 and when it is calmed down, dislocate the eye again and place an eye patch on his face for some days, and he should always be in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	 Then he should leave the house gradually, and return to his usual activities;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	 And one came to us who was from Yrach, and he told us that in his country they make an almagda pierce, which is used to draw water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I read of it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 and perhaps this is something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of the almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	 and they should be made of pure brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And the heads of them should be of this same subtlety, and the rears in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	 Sometimes they are born or attached to chariots in various ways, so that some seem like scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 And so there are of such where he has flesh with a fox-like color, and also flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	 In that case, with this type of flesh which is smooth and not rough, it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	 open his nostrils, and throw some incense on those smooth fleshes, and pull them out.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 then cut what you can hold with a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	 And if anything remains that cannot be cut, then open it with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	 And if pus forms there, or an abscess, then treat it as needed.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize until the pus is dried up and all the flesh removed, then apply a mixture of honey, vinegar, and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the honey works, and moisture comes to the palate, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	 And if moisture does not come out as needed, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	 Then it is necessary that you insert a small length of linen thread, and it should be knotted at each end by hand, with a space of one digit or less between the knots.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	 And let the patient put the head of the thread in his nostril as best he can, and pull gently until it comes out through the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	 And often children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 Then hold the end that comes out of the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and tie them together just like us who are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	 Do this until you know that the knots have destroyed that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and wet it in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	 Do this for three days or more, until the dressing has dissolved all remaining flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	 And then put in its place a plaster of lead for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 And this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, into which one distills the oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	 And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plaster, and with the same shape.
