et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	 And if you wish, make a closed plaster, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And it should have a handle for holding it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	 Often arises on the head of the nose a disease called "telul," and grows and becomes great immediately, to such an extent that it is a visible thing.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	 And therefore you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of it, then place on it the cautery or burning medication.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	 And if one delays in cutting it until it is large, then beware if it is hard, of foul color, or of poor quality.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	 Do not touch it with iron, for it is an infiltrated abscess. For when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 And if the abscess is of soft touch and not foul in color, and you see that it can be entirely cut out, then let the patient empty themselves and cut it without fear, and heal the place with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution for continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	 It therefore happens to anyone when this occurs, so examine whether the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and then bring the two lips together in a stitch, then cure it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	 and if the lips have already separated from one part to another, then it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of their heart until they heal, then bring the two lips together in a stitch, and hold them steady, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense on top.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster on the powders, and let it stay until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	 The method of sewing is such that you gather the thread:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	 or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the abdomen;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the lip abscess
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	 In many people, hard abscesses form within the lips, resembling millet seeds, some smaller and some larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	 then you must turn back the lips and cut above each knot, and take it with tweezers and chop it into small pieces;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 then fill the place after cutting with crushed vitriol, until the blood is stained.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and then apply oil of ashes, and dress the wound with dry materials until it heals.
de la char des gencives	 Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	 Often grows on the gums a skin called "albulus" by the ancients.
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	 so you must hold it with pincers, and cut it at its root, and let the wound or blood flow.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	 then apply powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders on the spot.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	 and if that skin returns after cutting, which often happens, cut it again the second time, and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	 if it does not return after cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 and these are the methods for cutting skin growths.
des sordens	 Of the teeth
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	 Sometimes there are gatherings at the roots of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	 And sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green due to decay, causing the gums to rot, and the teeth become foul-smelling.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	 Then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his chin should be in your sight, and clean the teeth or the scurf until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	 And thus do with blackness, greenness, and yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	 And if you remove what is there at the first root, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	 If not, then repeat the second day and the third, until you have cleaned everything.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	 And know that teeth require different types of instruments for cleaning, as the work demonstrates, because the type of scraper used to clean between the teeth is different from that used to clean behind them.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 And these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	 It is necessary that when you treat the tooth of its pain you delay drawing it as long as you can, for this should not be done.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to draw it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to pull out [the tooth], it is necessary that you be certain of the ailing tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	 Many times the pain deceives the patient and thinks that it is in a healthy tooth, and makes the good tooth drawn out;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	 yet the pain does not depart from this, as long as the evil is extracted, for we have seen it happen to these gentlemen;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	 and when you are certain of the painful tooth, then it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth on all sides with strong cautery to protect the gums from all parts;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	 then move it with your fingers or with fine tongs little by little and bit by bit, until it is well dislocated, then secure the tongs firmly;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 and let the head of the patient be between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it gently from each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	 And if the tooth is rotten and decayed, you must fill it with cloths where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	 and hold it firmly but gently with the tongs so that it does not break when pulled.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 and you must work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it, so that a part remains, and the patient suffers greater pain due to the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	 And beware that you do not act as the ignorant healers do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and do not bring about what we have described;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	 but sometimes bring about great diseases due to the roots that remain there, or for the cartilage they break, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	 and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine, or vinegar, and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	 and if there is a flow of blood from there, which often happens, then fill the place with pounded vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 and if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	 The forms of the instruments, with which one pulls teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	 and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And they should be of strong material so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made from good iron, and they should have teeth to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	 When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the place cotton moistened in butter for one day or two, until the place becomes soft, then insert the tongs which are called "algefri", with which the jaw seems like a beak of a hawk;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 And let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with these pincers, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," that is to say a forceps, in this manner.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	 And let it be thick and large enough so that it does not break, and if its root jumps out because of this, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 but if not, then help yourself with all the instruments by which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one uses this instrument which has two branches, as shown in this form.
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other iron implements that are before the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, whose form is shown here.
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	 And let this instrument be thick so that it cannot break, and know that there are many tooth instruments.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	 and likewise other instruments, which are not counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 and the wise master subtly finds his instrument by himself, according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, where it can, then look for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help with the gestures, by which here is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	 And they should be thick and well-gripping to hold the bone, that it does not slip, but can grip and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And then restore the place with suitable medications, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then remove everything from this tool.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	 When the teeth appear not according to nature, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth is new after the milk teeth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be sawn or filed.
adonques lou raie;	 Then extract it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this tool whose shape is like a small beak, and is made of iron at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the pliers little by little in many days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is visible so that it can be ground, then grind it with such a file as here is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	 And it is like the wax from which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	 And in wax little by little each day slightly, so that it does not move until it sets.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 Then plain it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then you must plane the roughness until it is smooth, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	 When the front teeth are loose, from a blow or fall, and the patient cannot chew what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with strengthening medicine, but it does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	 then they must be secured with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never moves; bidden:
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	 And let the thread be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	 And if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between two healthy teeth, then place the wires between the crooked teeth, whether there is one or more, until you reach sensibly to the other healthy tooth.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	 Then begin the covering again from the place where you began, and gently and wisely strain your hand until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 And let your lace be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	 Then cut the wires of the thread with wire clippers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that they do not injure the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	 And then he leaves it so tight as long as it can remain, and if it dislocates again, or the thread breaks, then he holds it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 if it remains and serves in this manner all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the meeting of two healthy teeth, and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	 And when the tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place, little by little, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from cow bone, and places it in the place where the defect is, and holds it as we have said, and remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper to suture the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	 Sometimes this string comes from under the tongue by birth.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	 or by an accidental wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	 and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hand, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	 then cut the nervous string widely, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is due to an accidental wound, then push in with the hook and cut widely that tendon;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	 and take care that the cut is not too deep, because of the artery that is beneath.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	 and when you have done this, raise the place with rose water and alum, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 And every night, the patient must comb out lice so that the wound cannot scab over.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	 And if bleeding continues, apply a poultice of vitriol to the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	 and if blood becomes thin, then cauterize with slow-burning cautery, which is good for that.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 then continue treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	 and if you see the wound turn black or hard, such that the patient cannot feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	 and if it is inclined to suppuration and there is moisture, apply onion juice, and open the wound with a fine probe, and drain it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	 And if blood overcomes you in your work, then apply vitriol broth until it is scorched, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the strength;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then lift him up on a bed of straw and silk, and treat him with other treatments until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 Of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	 Sometimes there appear in the throat boils that are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 if it is a hard abscess of little sense and dark color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	 And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the reason of bleeding;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	 but let it remain until it is dead, and then you will cut it off, or it would burst on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument to cut, but first look if the abscess is cooled and appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	 Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his head be in your hands, and he open his mouth and hold the instrument between his teeth, and press the tongue down under the whole instrument, which is thus shaped.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 and it should be of silver or fine tin as sharp as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	 When you press the tongue against the entire instrument and see the abscess, then take a hook and place it in the almond, and pull strongly upwards more than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	 And draw something from the cloth with it, then cut with the instrument, which has this form, like tongs.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And yet the heads are curved, and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this tool at hand, then take the tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	 And let them be cutting on one side, and notched on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold water and vinegar, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or boiled skins of pomegranates, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stanched.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then heal until it is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them in the same way as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed in her throat, namely one small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 and it had nearly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 et avoit ja bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez,
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	 Therefore, I hurried quickly and inserted into it one needle, then I drew it out, and I drew out with it a large amount of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	 Then remake another part in the other hole of the nose, and he opened his mouth and pressed his tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	 then they inserted a needle into these abscesses, and drained some of it, and only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	 and so the woman’s throat passage was unblocked, and she began to drink water first, then wine, and did not stop draining that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	 and the abscess always recurred and filled up the place that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	 then I inserted a device into it and cauterized it inside the throat
ensi demora sens croistre;	 thus it remained without growing further
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 And let these parts depart from me, and let God alone have made them after me.
de l’uve	 of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	 When the vein descends into the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 And if it is below, thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	 When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the cutting does not benefit, and you see that this abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then you must cover it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	 And that which is roundly assembled and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 And it is bloody or of the color of a rind or black, then you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, for its whiteness and length, let the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we made mention of before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Then insert the awl into the vein, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	 And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	 for if you cut more, then you harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and after the incision, use what we have said for the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you should use ingenuity for the cauterization to remove their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of cautery is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	 And it is that the patient places his head in your lap, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize with live coal water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And in the use of this instrument, here is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	 And at the tip it has a hair through which one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	 And the patient should be lying on their side so that the saliva and mucus run out of their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	 Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it soften and the stinging of the medicine subside.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	 And if you see (this), take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton hardens on the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	 And do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	 And if you need to start the cautery again with the medicine, then do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and let it be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	 This treatment is safer from incision than the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	 if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and lavender and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and add vinegar, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 And the pot should be well-glued with strong earth, and within the pot there should be an instrument fitted in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and one of the ends should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapors rise through the vein to the eye, causing the eye to become numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	 afterward it is often repeated until the eye dries out, and be sure not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen there.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And not to do so unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	 And if this instrument is not available, then take a reed and put inside the head a piece of eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 because the cliff of egg does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and this is a good cure together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	 Many times it sticks in the throat as a bone or spine of fish, or some other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	 so it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the thing;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	 and what does not open for you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	 perhaps then the hard thing will come out with the vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	 or if the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a lettuce root, or a morsel of dry bread; etti
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	 And attach a thread to the sponge
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	 And when it arrives at the place, it will harden, and then you will draw the thread.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 And if it does not come out due to what we have said, then take a lead instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	 And let the instrument be curved at the top so that it may enter the throat more easily, and have the tip raised.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	 And beware not to touch the epiglottis, so that all does not come out, nor push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	 And it is better that the patient himself places the instrument there, because he knows where the thing is hard.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 If he pushes downward, draw out the thread equally with all the instrument, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	 A certain time is treated the blood, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 And when this does not help at all, then look in the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you have pressed the tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the blood, draw it out with all the small hook, or with fine pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, then take a sharp knife, and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert into the hollow of the knife a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient is burning all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	 Then take full one vial of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without choking, and move it with his hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 And as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 Do this many times, for she will fall without hesitation.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	 And the method of fumigation is such that you take a pot with live charcoal in it, and let its lid be covered with a sieve pierced in the middle, and through that hole should be the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	 then cast your fumigation, and the patient should put the end of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that no smoke escapes, but it goes all the way to the blood vessels.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	 and now the blood will fall, and if it does not, then repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	 and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And then he will need it to come out by this means.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	 And the shape of the instrument used to draw blood is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers designed to enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	 And it should have the appearance of a seagull's beak and be rough like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot release.
et vez ci la forme:	 And see here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	 The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	 There are many similarities to an abscess, according to what is remembered hereafter in this book about one and the other, and they differ in penetration and cutting.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 And it comes in two types: one is exactly like it, and the other contains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second type is according to the location where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 for abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of fleshy parts are different from those that occur in joints, and each should be treated according to its own method.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	 And so with abscesses that one must not pierce, until the boil is dead according to its development;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And so with those that one must pierce when they are ripe and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near joints, and they are left until they become gangrenous all around, by chance then the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is why it causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	 Or if the abscess is near a principal limb, and you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	 Or if it is near the foundation (of the body), then one should pierce it as soon as it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	 And one should not pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for those near the foundation (of the body), lest it become gangrenous within and cause a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 And may not heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	 And it is necessary that you know the hour of the opening of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and the softening and the maturing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	 And you must make the opening seat itself in the most dependent place of the abscess, where it opens and moves.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And let the opening be long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no folding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those who are sick, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is healed with complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	 Car if you pierce it before this, then the body will be elongated with its poison, and it is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 And perhaps it hardens the lips and the depths of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess is perforated according to the width of the body, according to how much the limb needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	 And you must bring in small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	 and in large abscesses, large holes, and many splits according to the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	 And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the heart, and to cap;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	 When it becomes like a piece of cloth and is dead, then you must do as one does with children:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	 And if there are such that are split into three angles, and there are those which one covers like the leaf of myrtle, as with abscesses of the anus;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And if there are such cases where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar chopping.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	 Those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	 and when the abscess is large and it has formed a great pustule, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the pus at once, but only part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	 then pack the abscess until the next day, then draw something again.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	 do this several times from big to small, until all the pus comes out.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old and frail man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit may jump sometimes with the issue of the pus, which may cause the patient to die, and you may not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, cleanse the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	 and if it is a simple incision, then apply bandages of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	 and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then you must insert a bandage into each one so that they come together;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	 and if you have cut into the abscess some part of the skin and have pulled it over, then you must fill it with old cotton or shreds of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then remove, and treat with ointment until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and fresh water, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	 And if the bleeding continues, apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then you must put tents and cloths soaked in hot wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if it is summer, and the place is fleshy, then you must put on cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, up to the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then lance the abscess, and dry it, and treat it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	 Et cela doit être reconnu universellement dans le traitement des abcès :
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 and I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	 of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where headaches come from small abscesses, and they are similar to us who are in tissues, like the pustules of a chicken, and there are many such things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	 There are some that are greasy and such that contain moisture like pus.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 And there are those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the cut is such that you try with all the instrument that is called "scalpel," from which the form comes here after, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, then open it from above the lung.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	 And when the moisture is emptied, scrape off the skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left behind.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	 then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And those who remain from the night will run.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	 And then repeat the cotton treatment, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are sure that it does not remain from the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	 And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, then open it according to this shape, lengthwise;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	 and put your thumbs in it, and scrape it from all sides, and put all your effort into pulling the skin above where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the artifact gives you trouble, then do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for an abscess if it is pus-filled; cut and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And slice through the pus-filled and moist abscess, for it is lighter, because they are made of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	 And if any of these abscesses in the head where there is no moisture, and of these was the abscess that I opened in the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	 And I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if one had struck it, one would have made just as much of a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	 In other abscesses that come to a head, especially those which come at the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made in the most dependent place so that the pus may issue forth.
et les cure si com il covient.	 And treat it as is necessary.
des scrophules	 of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and they are many, and they are connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	 And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just like the node and the abscess of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And there are many similar scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Il y a de telles [dislocations] qui retiennent l'humidité, et il y en a de malveillantes qui ne veulent pas obéir à la guérison.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	 And in that which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and silent on all sides and is not harsh on the nerves of the neck nor on the artery nor on the passage, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	 so it is necessary that you cut above it, and scrape each part, and extend the two lips of the wound with tweezers if you need to, just as we have said in head abscesses;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not advance too far, lest you cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and that does not allow you to work, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that staunch blood, and bind the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And let it sit until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	 And when the blood has been staunched, then return to your work, so that you may complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 Then examine with your finger if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	 And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous swelling, then it is not fitting that you cut this swelling at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut all of the scrofulous swelling, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound, and stitch them immediately, since there should not remain any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 it is necessary that you aim to cut the root of it, and pull strongly, and stitch as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	 Those scrofulous ones that have swelling, prick them where they appear black;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	 and prick it as mentioned before, then bring tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and when the wound is well cleaned, then bandage it with a pleasant ointment until it heals.
de squinance	 of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	 The ancients spoke about cutting the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	 For those with scrofula, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" be cauterized;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 And one should not provide aid by this method, because all the veins and the flesh of the patient are affected in those who have an abscess that is hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	 It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four, a small transverse cut between the two circles or according to the size of the hyoid bone's cut, not at all in the laryngeal cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 And those veins are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	 And if the master is fearful, he should extend the skin of the throat to its full extent, then cut through the heart until it reaches the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	 And cleanse the vessels of blood, if you see anything, then cut the syphilis, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	 And it is proven by the incision of the phlegm from the throat which jumps strongly through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	 And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is feared, join together the two lips of the heart wound, and sew it alone without a dressing;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then administer medicines that produce flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Al-Zahrawi said that this should not be done until the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect has healed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	 Therefore, cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	 And for this reason, the elders commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed. And it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to suture and cauterize the wound until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	 I saw that a maiden took a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the tendons of the neck.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 And I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 Je découvris la plaie, et trouvai le sang qui en était sorti, et même s’il n’avait pas coupé de veine ni de canal fort, la gorge saignait abondamment à travers la plaie.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	 I hurried and sutured the wound and cauterized it until it healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	 And nothing happened to the maiden except that she was hoarse of voice, and later returned to her former state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 For this reason, I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should not be fear.
de la grosse gorge	 Of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a great abscess of blackish color, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	 and there are two types of them:
naturez, et accidens;	 natural and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 or the natural one has no fever.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	 And the accidental type is of two kinds, one of which resembles a boil on us, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	 and there should be fear, and it is not necessary to work with fire except on the small one, and test and search throughout the throat.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	 if you find it thus as we know fat, and it does not touch any vein, then cut it, just as one cuts the nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 and bandage it well immediately, and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	 There are many types of noses, all of which I will describe;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 and now it is necessary that I explain the entire difference between a nose and an outflow.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	 I say that outflow is hot and feverish as long as the inflammation has not passed and putrefaction is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	 With the nose, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a pus, which is its own bag and according to the color of the body, and it begins like a blister, and grows larger; }}}
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 And there are according to two similarities, either fat or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 Il is necessary that when you come to the cure of the nose, you test and examine first all the instruments called "entromissoire," according to what its form will be in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	 And the manner of inquiring about the abscess is that you take the most moist place you find on the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has reached the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 Then remove the probe, and take care not to allow air to enter.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	 If the running moisture has a color, then incise it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	 And if after the probe no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then incise it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape from each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the knot.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 And if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	 For if anything remains, the pain will return many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if there is a small piece left and the wound bothers you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and bind the wound, and apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and continue other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 And if the pain is great, then suture the two lips of the wound, and treat it as if it were an open flesh wound.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	 And if the swelling of the vein is troublesome to you or otherwise, then hurry and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two days or three, until the wound festers, and let the ebullition of blood subside.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 Then return to the top where some of the liquid remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	 Here are the forms of the intromissory instruments, and there are three types:
grans et moien et petit;	 large, medium, and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	 and there are three squares called "albaret," and one called "breb," and they come in three types.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	 large, medium, and small, to enclose the abscesses of fistulae;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	 and they are similar to the needles used for embroidery, made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow in color are more effective, coated with black lead to encase the roots of fistulae;
et sont de III manieres:	 And there are three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 great, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	 The shapes of boils are very similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	 great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	 and there are boils that have two curves of three kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	 and there are boils that have three curves, which are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	 and there are boils with two curves, and boils with only one curve, all of which are of three types.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	 The heads of these [tools] that are made are cutting, and there are such that cut only from one side, which are used for skinning fingers so as not to cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	 And from these intrusions are made the sleeves, so that the patient does not notice them when the abscesses open.
et sont de III manieres:	 And they are of three types:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	 great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	 And one should not use them except in fleshy places, such as the legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar locations;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 And sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the bark of figs, according to this form, to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And sometimes it is put in place that heals quickly of veins, and of the arteries, and sometimes it returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	 Sometimes men's breasts swell up when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts. ︎ Et c’est poour coi li preudome ne vont mie a leus nus quant il sont malades, por ce qu’il ne seent pas de la honte qui les est avenues par la maladie;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 And they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must proceed according to this form from this line .b. until .g..
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medication that promotes healing of flesh, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	 And if the breast sags downward and is softened due to its size as happens in women, then cut it into two ribs above, through two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	 So that one is held by the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g..
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then peel the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply that which we have said of stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed.
