Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	 And if there are hemorrhoids or abscesses in the rectum, let the enema be as fine as for a one-year-old child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the leather should be stretched:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	 We have already said in the section on the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 or we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicines according to their uses.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what they are made of.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	 The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or by spear or staff or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	 and which are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 And I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because their treatment will be discussed in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar things, and the skin is also torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	 If you do this immediately, heal with the cephalic method even if there is a little blood from the wound, and let the healing be opposite to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 and the patient should avoid eating too much wine and heavy food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	 And if he does not want to heal, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	 and place on the wound, if abscesses come there, only cotton soaked in rose oil or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	 and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and not moved by air, powder that I will mention a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if fire has moved it, then apply some poultices until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by sewing, as I will say for wounds of the belly, with the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	 If the wound is exposed to the bone and gaping, and only holds on by one spot, then chop it off;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 then treat the wound with medicine and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods such as heads and cooked wheat, also like beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	 And if you find rotting flesh and it reaches the bone, then cut off all the rot and cast it away, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	 and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which blood cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 and it is that you put this powder in before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	 And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	 take one part frankincense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	 blood of dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	 quicklime three parts, and make it into fine powder, and fill the wound, and hold it firmly until it becomes well-attached and joins all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	 and then bind it well, and leave it without unbinding, unless it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with only quicklime, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	 And if the wound has moved due to heat,
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	 but put on some poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it casts out the pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then continue with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	 And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 and I will tell you later about the fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	 of a neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the sinew of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	 If it is a nerve, then there is no other device than to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting on it, because this harms the nerves and causes them to withdraw;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	 And do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 but let the medicine be hot, like warm water mixed with rose oil, and wash the wound also in warm water, and other stones of similar manner, and moist dressings.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	 And if the wounds are deep and full of pus, then puncture it in a lower place.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	 And if the artery is cut and blood flows out, then restrain it, bind it, and cauterize if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	 And if the esophagus or the heart is cut and the passage is blocked so that food cannot pass, then suture the heart onto the spine of the neck, and do not touch the throat but replace it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then he holds it gently, and leaves it for some days, then treats it with dried onions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	 And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then he searches for it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	 And if there are bone fragments, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound rots, and is discharged and the exit cleared.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there are bones in the wound and it has an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the spear or dagger wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	 If it is a thrust from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if wind is coming out of the wound as the patient breathes:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	 Know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	 And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply the powder at the first hour, nor bandage it, for fear that the wound may bleed profusely, return to the heart, and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	 But apply an attractive ointment to it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	 And if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	 Thus, no spasm, trembling, heart strangeness, or drunkenness will come to him.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 And when you see the good arrangement, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Heal it then with bandages and other treatments until he is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	 And if she cannot heal and works again, know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	 If the treatment is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	 And if the wound is from the incision of a sword or knife, and it is simple, either on the back or behind, treat it as you would one in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	 If it is large, with stitches;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	 And if it is small, with powder. And if it is close to the bone and has chipped off pieces, clean the wound and remove the splinters if they are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	 And if they are not cauterized, let the wound suppurate, which will ease the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And for other wounds and other limbs, the judgment is the same as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 From the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	 The ruptures of the abdomen are great, moderate, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	 from the great wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, which causes their penetration.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	 And the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is harder to put the intestines back in, unless they are replaced immediately.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	 because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, and are harder to put back in, which is why the moderate wound is better, because it is easier to return the intestines to their place than with others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	 And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	 The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the sutures of other wounds of the body are two others which are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 And nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	 I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestine has come out, and it is a serious thing to put back, this is by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 Or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 Soak a sponge or cloth in warm water only, where you cook in hot water with hyssop and saffron and spikenard, and wash the intestines until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 and sometimes make this restraining wine, which should be drunk alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	 And when you see the swelling diminish, then moisten the intestines with water where mallows and marshmallows have been cooked, for through this the intestine is healed in a short time.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	 and if it cannot enter, then make an incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut out hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	 and the first treatment is that the intestine should be eaten, which no one should cut into unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	 And this is the tool to cut it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 if you cut inside at an angle and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened, and the intestine jumps out, then place it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you can, because this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	 When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	 and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the feet higher than the parts below, and also if there is a turn of the belly in one of the two parts, then pay attention to this: that the injured part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And thus it is necessary to proceed as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	 In small wounds, apply what is prepared, then have between your hands one skillful minister who holds all the turn at his hand, and gather the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	 And this is the common way of stitching, which is that you take a needle or several, according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingerbreadths from the top of the wound, and there you insert a needle with a strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	 and pierce the two heads of the leather with the two heads of the thread, which is underneath the leather inside, so that you make it pierce from this side, and join the two heads of the thread together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	 then pull a double thread around the needle on two sides, then join the two heads of the wound together, and leave two fingerbreadths, and insert another needle there.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	 Then take the thread of the needle just as you made the first needle, and do not stop making them according to your need for needles, until all the wound is restricted.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	 And let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick, because fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	 Therefore, they must be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	 And it is not necessary to insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and widen the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	 And then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not wound the patient while sleeping, and put caps or bandages on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	 And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, for it allows a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	 The second stitch is common and consists of assembling the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the flesh together with one needle with a strong, medium-sized thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	 And when you have passed these four heads all together, then bring the needle back to the place where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	 And leave a space between each stitch the thickness of two small fingers.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 This stitch men know, and I sewed a wound that one man had in the belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it protruded the intestines well two palms long, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestines to him after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed until fifteen days, and I cared for it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 And I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and I washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing.
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 Take the needle, and pass it from the outside to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 When it has pierced the skin straight on straight, leave the end of the silk or thread where you passed the needle on the outside, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 And the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and that you leave one time the thread on one side, and take it up again from another, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is done like some do, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Insert a needle into one end of the thread close by, and make it pass through that place only, and leave the two ends of the thread;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 then turn the needle and make it pass from the outside part until inside, to the two ends of the thread;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then have one pierced from the outside part to the other inside, in two other places of the temple that are on either side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 And this is the method of suturing and it is the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said these words, and some attest to it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, with thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 And one needle must be pushed from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 And know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more difficult than from other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before heat has moved it, then set aside burning the interior, and the skin.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 then apply powder of stag beetle, and if heat has moved it, then apply some ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 and stitch the threads, and let the silk and the thread be joined together;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 and if you do not have medicine, then apply, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 For you do not need any other medicine in many situations when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 And if you doubt that the wound will affect the main limbs, then you must soak a light linen cloth in temperate oil or rose oil, and place it around the joints, and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 And if he feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this often happens, then enema him with lukewarm black wine, and likewise if the putrefaction reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 And pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the entrails come out of the wound, then push them back in just like the intestines, while they are still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if it is old and turned black or dark, then you must tie the black area so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then cut that which is between the ligaments, and place the two ends hanging from the lower part of the wound until enough to lighten the extraction when the projectile falls, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the bursting of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are cut and the wound is small, it can be healed in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which came the excretions and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I applied care according to my ability, and did not stop refining until he was healed, and the place was joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I saw it join, I feared that the patient might have an ailment in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and there was no illness there, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 take forceps with large jaws, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the forceps has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it closes its mouth upon them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 and then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then place another forceps in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is fully seized;
et cout la plaie.	 And cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 If the heads enter the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, one can tie off the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 Take the head of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie a fine twisted linen thread to the head of this thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew up the intestines, and bring it back to its proper place;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 And this manner of suturing for wounds is nothing but according to the way of confidence and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 And if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal grooves, there is no cunning or skill, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 You should know that any wound or abscess, when it bursts open, is universally called a "fistula," and likewise when it is incised and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And a fistula is according to the truth a hard and white nodule, where one does not feel pain, and it is also rooted like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 and sometimes in clear fluid, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 sometimes deep, and other times shallow;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 and I have already spoken of it in the section on wounds, that any wound that does not heal, and there is no flesh there, it is only due to one of the NINE causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 that is to say, because of the weakness of the blood or body; ︎
ou por sa malice;	 or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 or because there is hard flesh within it, and on the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 where there is too much flesh;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 where the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 or because the corruption is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 or because in that region, digestion is slow, healing is delayed, and swelling is natural;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 or there are veins or bones there:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula caused by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Know that a fistula can occur in any part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 because there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the sinus, or the intestines, or the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And so for those who come to the property of the main limb, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 And all fistulas that are of this kind are of severe curing, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a needle of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, then prick it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is crooked, then seek out a subtle needle of lead, for lead bends more easily around the crookedness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has multiple holes and you cannot easily locate it with needles, then administer an enema through one of the holes, for moisture thus cuts from one hole to another, and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then carefully seek with your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it has been severed completely, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foreign body and the rotten flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep in a straight place, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then put wet bandages soaked in healing water on it, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then he applies onion-like dressings to clean flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize it as we have said; and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If a vein or nerve injures a principal member, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape until all the corruption is removed, then treat with flesh-like dressings until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 and if it does not heal and pus forms again as before, know that you have not yet reached the end.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 then expose and seek until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it is healed this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 But if not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is a little bit of bone corrupted and you can remove it with tweezers, then remove it with the appropriate instrument for that purpose; and if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving none behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 And if moisture opposes you and there is no mistake or fear, then cut and remove the flesh and skin, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something that induces putrefaction on the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be easier to obtain;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then remove the flesh only up to the blackness, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 and if there is a great part of corruption, reaching as far as the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 then it must be sawn and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 There was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from something inside the body, so that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and he had no reason to open it. ething
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 but the doctors in their folly worked so much on it that they opened the abscess, and a lot of matter came out, and it became a fistula, and many perforations appeared, all of which released pus and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 and many doctors tried to cure it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what came out through the perforations was very foul-smelling;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 and the body of the young man became red, and he had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came up against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 I hurried then, and I cut into one of the perforations until I uncovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupt and decayed, and the corruption reached as far as the inside of the bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I saw that the bone was rotten, and I thought there was no other corruption except for what I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 and then I reopened [the wound], and discovered the bone as before, and found that the corruption continued in the bone, and saw it, and then removed it, and tried to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of bone, and then drew it out completely, then treated it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 and it was quickly healed and closed, and I did not need to reopen the wound except for the weakness of the patient, who could not tolerate [it], and out of fear that I would cause his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Car for the evacuation of blood, he often bled, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or opposite effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take a ligature, and tie it to the end of the bone that is protruding, and command someone to pull it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and put another ligature of thicker linen on top of the first ligature, and tie it onto the flesh that is above the bone, and pull upwards so that you draw the corrupted flesh downwards, and expose the flesh in the place where you want to set the bone, so that the suture does not injure the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 and place a heated iron or board under the bone to completely cover the corrupted flesh; 
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 and it is necessary to set [the bone] as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to set [it] again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is rotten, and does not open, and the rot is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then place the ember underneath, and then let there be silk from one part to the other of the rot, and let the length of the silk be equal to the length of the rot, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the rot is in the joint, then cut away the rotten joint, and silk the bone on which it adheres from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 And if the rot is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut it out.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 And if the rot is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must seek out that rot and see how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And cleanse it in all ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 And know that the incisors and the saws to cut these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their fineness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 And for this reason it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 And know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the kinds of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If you think about the instrument of which you have need according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	 of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head swells either from within or from without;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 and when you have treated that corruption with the care of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death or the greater harm of the loss of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and then swells after the blackening, for this corruption of the limb spreads from limb to limb, and affects the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 if you are quick to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some poisonous animals, such as a sea scorpion or viper, and similar things, if the corruption is at the base of the finger, then cut it off, and do not give it space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it goes up to the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not spread to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 and if it comes to the arm, then cut it with a knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 and if it goes beyond the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of his strength.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 and do likewise when the corruption comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 and if it goes up into the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other strategy than to leave the patient to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 And the manner of the cut or of the silk member is such that you tie it above and below, and one assistant extends one end of the ligature downwards, and another assistant the other ligature upwards, and you sever the flesh that is between the two ligatures in a place one finger wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 then cut or silk, and place on each side a piece of linen, so that the silk does not touch the healthy flesh, and cause the patient to have another wound and abscess there.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if blood flows as you work, then quickly cauterize the place, or apply some restraining powders on it.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 Et je te dirai que cela arriva à un homme dans son pied.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 Il lui advint une tache noire qui ressemblait à une brûlure de feu, et cette corrosion commença d'abord dans son gros orteil du pied, jusqu'à ce qu'elle envahisse tout le pied.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 Et quand l'homme vit la corruption, il se hâta de couvrir le pied, et fut guéri.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 Et longtemps après, la corruption revint dans le gros orteil de la main. Il vint à moi, et je lui appliquai des remèdes répulsifs après avoir nettoyé le corps, mais il ne put arrêter la corruption.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 Et il demanda que je lui coupe la main, ce que je refusai car j'espérais encore pouvoir repousser la matière.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 And I doubted also that if I cut his hand, he would not die, for the virtue of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 And he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and struck his hand with a sword, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And I have not told this account except for what one must do if needed elsewhere.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a large gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 And then they round and pierce, and the pus jumps out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 And the skin above is as thin as fine cloth, and it does not run to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such an illness is called «sain», and is not called «fistula».
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 But if it is so elongated that it comes up to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 and the skin is such that you cut around all of that skin, even when it is thin, like a sheet;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and it does not become infected due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you are confident that the skin will become infected, and the infection is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clyster in this manner:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 look to see if the breast is large, and the discharge from it is of foul odor, then treat it with a clyster made of Egyptian medicine thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 take asafoetida, and oil, and lead oxide, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 And then take some according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and use it as an enema in the breast, and constrain the anus;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 And leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by pressing out.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 Do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the pus removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 And sometimes use an enema of ash water when this medicine is not present, and it should be that you take ashes from a vine stick, pour water over them, then filter, and use as an enema until you know the breast is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then enema with honey and water where there is a little bit of lead.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 ou you clean it with honey and mixed wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the wound dry.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this, and you are confident that the wound is well purified, then you cleanse it with that which produces flesh in it. It is that you take a definitive plaster and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken about the properties in the section on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 and if the hole in the wound is small and the tip of the syringe cannot enter, then widen it with an iron hook slightly, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilic ointment until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too wide, then cut it and leave only as much in place so that the suppository can enter, and if the opening through which the bowel exits is above, then cut it or move it to a lower place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the bowel is fully out, do not let any flesh enter;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 and if you cannot cut the skin as you see fit, then prepare it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place there is, for when the bowel is fully out, do not let any flesh enter; and if you cannot cut the skin as you see fit, then prepare it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 so that the bowel runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowel there;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 And take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and place them on a linen cloth that covers all the wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 Then cut a piece of cloth the size of the wound and a little larger than before, then place a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and put it on the wound to relieve the pain, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 And the one that is on the wound, remove often to relieve the pain, and know what comes out of the pain, whether it is poison or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 And beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that leaps onto the wound, know that the wound is already healing, and health approaches.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 And then unbind it in the morning of the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the breast throws up undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons have passed after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men in whom the flesh grows late in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 And if the undigested matter comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 And if the breast is slow to heal and is distant (from healing), then apply drying moist substances that are dry in virtue, such as refined ointment, for it contains a large part of copper, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take refined ointment, made with rose oil, and wash it with equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	 then mix and apply it
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 and this same mixture works better when onions are not present, or take myrrh, aloe and incense, grind them up, powder them over the honey while it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 and then use it as an ointment, apply it to the chest, sometimes you can add a long arrowroot and celestial lily roots, which are like vetch flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 and use them either as single ingredients or in mixtures:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 grind them up, make a powder, put it on the honey that I mentioned earlier, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 and if the treatment is prolonged and it is not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made an impression on the bone or hard members or ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 Si li cures de la fistule, si com nos avoms dit ci devant.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the fingertip abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Panarice is an abscess that forms under the nail of the finger or toe, or sometimes in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 and when it is neglected, and no care is taken of it, then this abscess comes about, and it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it will destroy the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 and the corruption reaches the bone, causing a stinking pain, and the nail of the toe becomes wide, and its color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off with an iron knife all the remaining excess of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 Cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 And if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to prick it and wound it, then you must place a thin strip of wood under the nail so that it no longer touches the flesh, and push it up, and carefully and lightly cut away that part of the flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it away and pull strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone remains there, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if you see that the finger is rotting, then cut it off at one of its joints as described above, then heal it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if he is wounded and bruised and feels great pain, then you must heal him first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 then cut the nail of the sputum-making finger diagonally on top, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 and if it happens, then apply something soothing on top.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two thumbs that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshly, and sometimes there is one with bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and sometimes they grow from the root of the joint, or their birthplace is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 He who is born from any knot of the two does not move, and he who is born at the junction of the two, perhaps will move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cutting of the one who is fleshy is light in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 cut him at his root with a broad sputum-making finger.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	 If you hold [the shoulder].
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the case of one who is born or should at the anus, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The swelling that comes to the two together comes from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 It is necessary that you cut this seam, so that they may return according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 then place between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Or you can place between two thin plates of lead, until the site is healed, as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly one of his fingers comes with the palm, cut that joint as needed.
des vils	 of the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 Veins are large openings filled with melancholic superfluities, which come into many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 and it happens more in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to him, and then treat him with a plaster.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 one is that they are cut, and the black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And the other way is to lift the vein and draw it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The cut is made in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 first soak the patient's leg in very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin, then press on the patient's leg from above the hip to below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one of these three places with a wide incision, and lift out and draw forth strongly the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 and then tie it off, and instruct the patient to eat nourishing black food.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And the evacuation and bleeding restart when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The healing of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 shave the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and rinse the leg with hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 and if you do not have a bath, then heat it at the fire, and then cut towards the vein from the ankle to the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 then remove the skin at the corner, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 And it is seen red and black, and when it enters the leather it seems also like a bleached rope.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then push the thread down until it is raised from the leather, and then fold it at the corner lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the leather on the vein until it appears, then raise it to the lace, as you have done, and fold it at another corner, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then cut another piece, or several if you need it, then lift it, and cut at the finger of the foot, then draw it and lift up to the second piece.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then draw it from piece to piece until it comes out completely, then cut it off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 And if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a needle with all its strong thread doubled, tie and pull it, and insert under the skin, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and this will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have pulled it all out, then place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the vessel is twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it obliquely, but do not cut it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And there you draw as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The form of the iron with which one cuts the vessel is curved and does not cut through, so that it does not cut the vein;
