et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and is of a large curve, for if it were delicate, it would cut the vein. But let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is inserted in the legs, in hot places where no grass or tree grows, and in earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 And perhaps it can appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms are inserted between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that it comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of cloth from one and a half to two and a half (inches or centimeters unclear), including the knot, and let the cloth hang down the leg. And every time some point escapes, you wrap it again around the cloth, and the knot;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, then cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, and do not cut it at its root until all of it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction in that place, and a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 Therefore it is necessary that it be drawn out little by little until the end, and not leave anything in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 And sometimes this vein, when it is drawn from five palms in length, or from ten, and a man came to me, for whom it was twelve palms long, and when you cut it, then it throws out one or two drops of blood, and it pierces through to the bottom, so that all comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply medicines that prevent corruption every day, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And sometimes this vein has fewer drops of blood, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there come many drops, from which it jumps drops;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens often to oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes through the entire body ascending and descending, and one feels it well when moving from limb to limb, until it wears away the skin where it goes, and then leaps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 It is infected by the putrefaction of certain humors, just like come worms and snakes and leeches and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see it being healed and pulled out, one cannot do so except when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 thus it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tie very tightly, then cut above and pull strongly, and if the pus has entered deeply into the flesh, and you do not find it, then burn it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 and the greatest harm that it does is that it infects the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, restrain strongly under it with a scourge, then cut above, and pull strongly;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 and the patient must use body cleansing with dissolving medicines for evil humors, and refrain from rotten foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in certain members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 And I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And soon after, I saw it move up to the shoulder like a worm, faster than anything, just as quick silver moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain left that place and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a little while later it ran through her whole body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then she told me that it was always turning around her body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 I greatly wondered how it moved from one member to another, for I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Nevertheless, I had seen many who wished to move pain from one place to another, but I had not seen it as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 And I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and for this reason the forced winds appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 But it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and abundant veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then quickly cut above and below it, and then chop until that forced wind issues forth from the place.
et cauterize le leu;	 And cauterize the place.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it as you would those who suffer from flatulence, such as stinking pills, and serapinus pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Arrows vary according to their appearances and the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The differences in them is that there are some which have large points, small ones, hooked and straight.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And some that have two prongs, and those that have tongues, and those in which there are fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 And if it falls into any member, it falls according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 Or in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it falls then into any part of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 If it is necessary for you to beware of the extraction of this arrow, because death follows in many forms.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 And when this ill sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And the signs of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and there is a strong odor above the brain, are when the patient experiences loss of vision in one eye, dizziness, fainting, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And perhaps there is a strong odor from the nose or the ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 And perhaps he loses his speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 And from the wound comes white moisture like a finger's tip, and it leaps out like charcoal's ember.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And if this sign appears to you, then avoid treating it, and remove the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The signs of an arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And perhaps the arrow moves like a finger, and black blood flows from it, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting occurs.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of an arrow that never exits is when without plain foam it comes out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if the arrow falls into the kidney cover, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 And casts great groaning and great pain and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested meat will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and some feces come out through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck, throat, shoulders, arms, spine of the back, chest, hips, legs, and similar members, are safe according to several conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man whose arrow fell into the forehead at the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I tried it, and drew it out from another side under the skin of the ear, and he was cured without difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And drew from a youth an arrow that fell into the eye under the eyelid underneath, and the arrow was bent, and he could not grasp it except for the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, all of light iron without wings;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The youth was healthy, and no misfortune befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And he drew an arrow from his throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic in origin:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I shaved the beard, and was subtle enough to draw it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And I drew an arrow from a man, which had fallen into his belly, and I thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut around the arrow, and hooked it, and drew it out strongly, and he had no misfortune.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And I saw a man upon whom an arrow had fallen on the back, and the wound was closed up; etti ne le pooit traire parmi, et n’ot point de mavais accident. etti je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And the arrow remained within him, and it did not change its natural dispositions at all, nor was there any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And he saw another man, upon whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and it remained thus without causing great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And he shot an arrow at one of the king's nobles, which had fallen into his nose and was slightly slanted towards the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was completely bent.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was called to tend to it after three days had passed since it fell. xspace Et mout d'autres semblans.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I examined it all with great care and did not feel any (pain or resistance); xspace et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt a prickling pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was from the arrow's tip; I placed on the spot an astringent and digestive plaster, so that the place would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And the place of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I put the plaster on for fewer days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose.
et il le me dist.	 And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I placed a corrosive medicine on the wound for several days until it was open, and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which had lodged in place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 Then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that sharpened instrument, until the head of the arrow became clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 and the deadline was exceeded by about four months, and then the wound opened where I inserted the pincers, and I pulled it from one side and another, but it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 then I did not stop trying and devising ways to use instruments until one day I took it with well-made pincers, according to the shape that will be shown at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 Or I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you direct your care towards what I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise master comprehends well even a small thing, and that which is present and failing, finds nine works, and nine instruments, for the practice of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows should not be removed from the members into which they are thrust except according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which comes out through the same place it entered is an arrow entering fleshy places, and this can sometimes be done now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and the exit is lightened.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and soften it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And then it will jump out, and if it does not, pierce around with all the delicate forceps until the place around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and goes into one of the brain cavities, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned happen to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 Do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, death occurs.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 Et si la flèche n'est pas fichée trop profondément dans l'os uniquement, et ne parvient pas jusqu'à la moelle, et que le patient reste quelques jours sans incident grave, alors utilise l'instrument de traction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot come out by force, then administer herbs around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that one cannot see it, then seek it out along its entire length;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, then widen it until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 and draw out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, then remove the flesh on both sides of the barb as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow so that you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And be careful not to break the arrow when you pull it out, so that you do not wound more severely.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it in one go, leave it until the place around is rotten, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if the flow of blood troubles you, then use what we have said about treating it in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And take care of the incision of the nerve and vein, and contrive how you can most safely pull out the arrow, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And place the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that can be done, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow that comes out from another part, where it protrudes somewhat, or the skin is swollen in that place so that it is clearly visible or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Cut then upward, so that the pincers can grab it, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot come out, then leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 and if there is the shaft of an arrow in it, push all of the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 and if the shaft falls out and you see that a pushing instrument is needed, then administer an instrument with a groove in it so that the tip of the arrow enters into the groove of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 and then push strongly, and if the arrow is grooved, then push an instrument with an entering point into it to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if an arrow falls into the chest or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is near, and you can strike above it, then strike.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And be careful not to strike the vein or the nerve, and then extract [the arrow], and then suture the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And continue the care until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the pincers used to extract arrows is like a bird's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the tip for pushing [the arrowhead] is like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 Li forme des tenailles pour pousser et pour tirer, elle est ainsi :
des voinnes dou cors communes	 de vignes du corps communs
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 There are 31 ways to heal wounds, with 16 being in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 Two temples after the ears, which are called "herbish".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 et les deux artères qui sont dans les deux temples apparentes;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 And the two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspirants";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 et la voine qui est au milieu du front;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 et la veine qui est au sommet du nez;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 and the two jugulars that are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins that are commonly healed are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 the first is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 And the way is called "fasting," and it is composed of cephalic and basilic, and common people call it "vein of the heart.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 And the basilic is in the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the scapula, and it is that from which one bleeds, which clearly opens on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the salvatella is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg and in the foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 One is under the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second is called saphena, which is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 And the vein called "nesse," which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 and there are three veins beneath them in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 and the quality of the bleeder, as I tell you, is that you lift the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 then have the patient squeeze his neck with one hand, so that the two veins behind the ears appear in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 pinch them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, prick it there;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lance, and pass it under the vein to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein, and cut well through the skin and the vein in two places, and make the blood flow out as much as you wish.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then constrict it and bind, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 And I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples serves for ancient migraine, and headache, and customary ophthalmia, and the body of acute tears in the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the qualities of the bleeder are as I say.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 And it is that the patient should draw his neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feel your thumb under your toe, then sign of the rest.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then lift the heart up onto the vein at the top of your toe, and push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and cut it, as you have done with two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then unbind the patient, and put your toe on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and then bandage it firmly, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 And we have spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The bleeding from the forehead vein is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic for ancient face diseases, and for migraines, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And its nature is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Then take the instrument called "fosseur," which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or another object, and allow the blood to flow in the quantity that you desire;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then release the patient's neck and tie off the vein until it is healed, and sometimes use a wide flame to complete the task.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 However, it should not be that the flame is too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 and cut at an angle, for the bone is nearby, and perhaps the flame will break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in two lids helps with the eyes, and with tinea, and with redness, and with the little corner of the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 And the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient should twist his neck with some rope as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then bleed, and let the bleeding be deep, a little long and a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the flame is delicate, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make the blood flow until you have enough, and then tie it off with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The bleeding of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and sudden madness, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 and the nature of the vein is such that the patient tightens his neck, then press your left hand against his nose, take a long, thin flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for a night, because it heals very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The vein of the two temples helps in the constriction of the head, and at the beginning of paralysis, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosions, and in shingles, and in inflammations;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 And the quality of the wound is such that the patient should move his neck from one side to the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 And let the master stand on the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then open the vein from the length of a span widely, then draw out the blood temperately, as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then repeat with another vein, then untie the bandage, and press gently on all the veins, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And leave it until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bleeding of the wounds of the lips above helps to swell in the mouth, and to corrupt the gums, and to split the lips, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the quality of the bloodletting is to make the patient sit before you and draw out his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is in the right lip and the other in the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 Then cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the bloodletting under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue follows the bleeding of the cephalic [vein], and this is for narrowing the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 and the nature of the physician is such that the patient lies in your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 heal one and not the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins of the knife with which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 either by pricking with the whole flame of a large myrtle or an olive tree, as sharp as cutting knives, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The form of the martin flame is very famous, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary for opening the full veins filled with thick visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 et c’est la forme du fléau malaire:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more subtle and pointed, and it is for healing subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The saphenous vein of the leg, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases under the throat, and in the neck, and in the foot, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And it is necessary for the healer to cauterize wisely, and to beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow, then he must cauterize it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the flame should not be pointed, but rather shaped like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 And if the leg vein does not open clearly, then you must squeeze it and change another [vein].
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 Where you wish to take some of his blood, or you heal the vein in its place within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	 it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 and apply the flame cautiously, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you wish to locate the vein, it is necessary first that you stretch out the arm so that you can touch the spot until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 then mark the spot with a knife and then tie off the arm and cauterize the vein with the flame carefully.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the spot swell, for it is from the artery.
eschui la donques.	 avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it spurt upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Hasten then, and place your finger on it for a while, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 if his arm falls, let him remain still and not move it, the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and hold it steady, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the blood does not clot and it overcomes you, and the physician is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, because the head of the vein will recede.
et estainche li sans.	 and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And take a strip of linen, and tear it, and take one half and tie it firmly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if the blood clots, that is good. ‌
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If not, treat it as we have said with powders that staunch blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the stanching is not difficult in many cases due to the small area of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The bleeding from the middle of the wound helps in that it draws blood from the top and bottom because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 And the bleeder should be cautious because of the nerve that is underneath, and if it goes too deep and finds the nerve, and swells up, then stanching will be difficult, and possibly it cannot be staunched.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must stanch it with the cautery instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And let the nerve slip as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The sinus of the cephalic vein helps, for it draws blood from the head and aids in sight;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is necessary to incise in the pomegranate flame or in the myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because under it there are neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 However, one must seek the lightest place, and do not worry if one misses the first time, and start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And sometimes the spot swells in some men when they miss the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you should know about incising is that an incision is only done to preserve health and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are in the body:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 which are known as: cephalic, fastus, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And one should bleed at the beginning of spring to autumn, and in winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but should be done by day or night, at any hour and in all circumstances;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And it is not appropriate to bleed children under fourteen years of age, nor pregnant women until the seventh month. xspace
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 Nor should the elderly over sixty years old be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And when someone wishes to be healed in any way, it is necessary for them to cleanse the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not attract the harmful superfluities from the intestines into the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 nor will someone be healed if they are too full of food, or drunk, as long as they remain so, or if they are suffering from dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 and if one wishes to be healed after suffering from colic, vomiting, diarrhea, increased frequency of intercourse for women, and labor, vigil, fasting, or any other loss of strength due to a weapon or bodily illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then refine the humors, if the blood is thick, by food and drink and medicine, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then enter the bath, if nothing prevents you, to refine the blood, and heal the wound of the worst part by the third time, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And guard yourself that day against work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 And be happy and joyful, and let the healer's hand be higher than that of the person being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then pull on the ligament moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and are felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 then moisten the cauterizer with a little old oil, then place his left-hand thumb on that vein below the spot where he wants to cauterize, so that the vein does not burst or leak during the operation.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that flow like cords to the cauterizer, and some are full of windiness, so that when one applies the flame, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is among them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow; therefore, it is necessary for the cauterizer to be knowledgeable in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein opens on the first try, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 if not, then start again a little below or above that place, quickly, if the place is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the place is inflamed and the patient is frightened, let him wait for a day or two and do not tie up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 perhaps an abscess will form there
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 and do not enter into a bath, then start the bleeding again if he wishes to.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 and if the opening is small or the blood flows gently and you doubt that enough blood will come out as you wish, then pierce that same opening with all the flame straight on.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 and do the work quickly, before the place becomes inflamed;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the place inflamed, do not restart the bleeding, and apply a poultice of linseed oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place lies the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And so administer linseed oil to each bleeding you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 and the same thing acts as a poultice and heals from them, when it is placed on the place.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 if it thins the blood and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 And if an abscess forms, which happens often, especially when it is not severely bled except for that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place on the spot a sponge moistened in water and salt, a little hot, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains in the place after several days, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, put on some aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And often an abscess and swelling occur at the base of the vein:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 Then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the touch, then this swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Avoid putting anything on it that we have mentioned, because by chance some of the blood may be coming from an artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 But make a dry plaster to harden the area, and then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw from each one of the blood according to the quantity of its power and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 Because if the blood is black, let it out until it becomes red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 And if you see it thick, let it out until it is refined.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 And the one who is strong and healthy, if he needs to have blood let out, make him a larger wound, and the fire should be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the weak one, do the opposite, and he should be bled frequently and often, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this method of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is worth more than the long or wide incision for bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 Et à celui dont le corps manque de force, il faut donner du pain imbibé dans du jus de pommes.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If he is hot, then draw blood three or four times; and if he is of a cold temperament, then before the bleeding, let him eat bread soaked in muscadine syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he bleeds from the wound after much blood loss, he must drink broth of meat and subtle scented syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wishes to bleed from the arm and bleed again later, it is necessary that when he has been weakened by much bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time, according to his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if someone wishes to bleed from the arm after the first bleeding and he has a strong body, then let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And if someone wishes to bleed from another part of the body, he should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 Because there is much blood within the body which has already heated up, causing fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 therefore it is necessary to draw a large quantity of it, and widen the opening so that it can drain fully.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 Then, after you have considered all the conditions of bleeding and placed your hand on his pulse when he is bleeding, so that death does not come in place of blood, and this often happens when the bleeder is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 And it is not necessary that when you see the arm dislocated, and blood comes out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press very hard;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 nor if it is bent, to extend the arm quickly, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 but let it remain until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 or you point it with the tip of the flame, so that the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein flows out, and place a poultice made in water on top, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if there is a need to bleed a second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The veins in the arms are healed in the vein of the head because they are closer.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the manner of healing is that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the fingers turn red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 then it should be tied moderately, so that the veins appear well, then heal across now, not widely nor lengthwise;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 And let the opening be wide, and let it be cauterized well near the joint of the hand, and if pus cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 And if it is in summer, then do not put the hand in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the cautery of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no major artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The cautery of the little finger of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Hold the hand tightly and put it in hot water until the vein swells, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 And if you slash it across, and if you cut it all around, then it will not hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not go too deep, for the nerves are bare under all the flesh, and then put your hand in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn as much blood as needed, then put oil and seal on the vein to heal quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The bleeding from his left hand is as valuable as the disease of the mouse, and does everything just as I have told you concerning the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The bleeding from the spleen is as valuable for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient should put his foot in hot water, and rub on the wound until it breaks, and bind over the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And the wound is at the ankle, and above the foot go many rains;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 cut it then in the widest part of the vein, or at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 And if you treat it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut through them as in slicing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in water, and let the wound drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 And if the cutter fails the first time, then begin again a little higher, for the place is salted;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 Nor doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the ankle of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its bleeding is good for hip pain, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of this cutting is such that the patient enters into a bath, and pulls four fingers above the ankle by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 And if it opens, then cut in all the ways that you can, and by slicing through;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And it is better that you cut it, for the place is safe, and she is very responsive in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you cannot find it, then cut some of its skin that is open on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 and make the blood flow as much as you see fit, and then unbind the bandage, and apply cotton and bind it on;
ele est maintenant sanee.	 she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of cupping therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Cupping glasses are made of horn, or iron, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this cupping which is done without pricking is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 where it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 and venesection which is done by bleeding and bloodletting, is performed in fourteen places on the body, one of which is entirely at the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	 and another is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and two others on each side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and a cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and a cupping glass on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and a cupping glass on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and cupping glasses on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and cupping glasses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 and cupping glasses on both ankles; etime
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 and venesection does not draw blood, except from the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken at all, as one would do with a venesection of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it is not necessary that she be administered, neither by any fire nor without fire, in any disease caused by excess, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to ventose, or for custom, administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, in the middle, and at any time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 For there are some who, when they need to be ventosed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 And there are those who find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness of vision.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 And there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and vomit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 and there are some who dream of seeing blood and wounded and dead things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order them to be bled after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The draining of the nose also helps with the headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 and this draining is in place of the draining of the head, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion or have catarrh, because it does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And he who often bleeds from it becomes forgetful, and because of this one should place the cupping glass a little lower out of fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 The draining in the neck is in place of the draining of the head and the nose, and for this reason it is useful for constriction of the bladder, and for cleaving the passage of the spleen, and for constipation, and for fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 And there it is necessary to apply little by little, for if it holds too firmly, then it injures the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosations at the second rib of the neck are good for headaches, and migraines, and for strangulation, and for toothache, and it is in the place of the basilica's sinus.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And it is necessary that you instruct the patient to press his hand firmly, so that he does not cut the artery and does not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 The ventosations under the chin are good for mouth diseases, and for rotting of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 And it is in the place of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The ventosations of the shoulders are effective against diseases caused by heat and inflammation.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 The cauterizations of the ribs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 And instruct the surgeon not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and beneath are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 The cupping glass that is on the buttock is worth as much for hemorrhoids and diseases below, and it should be large, and made of copper, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 And perhaps, if it were too delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 And it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The cupping glasses on the legs are effective, for they draw blood from the whole body, and they are worth as much against old pains of the kidneys, and the spleen, and the bladder, and they remove phlegm.
