et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 And they are in the place of two spleens and two ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The manner of placing the cupping glass is to place it first empty, and suck immediately, and place quickly, and move equally, and do not stop doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and apparent is the redness of the blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 then burn, and replace the cupping glasses, and pay attention to the constitution of the body, for there are some who have dark flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 then it is necessary to burn only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deep puncture;
et suce legierement.	 and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the blood is thick, one must strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 the first time to make a subtle incision for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the blood is very thick, one must strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only need to do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we want a lot of blood, we must repeat often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the outcome is that the heart should be pierced suddenly. And for those who have thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, it is necessary to anoint the places of the cupping glasses with aperitive and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 if it is in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if one treats a person with thin skin and large pores, there should be no oil applied to it, but it must be washed after being fumigated with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And one who has much moisture should use aloes, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those who have excessive waste should rise with old wine, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and it is not appropriate to cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 and he should not sleep after cupping, and he must be clean when he is to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And watch out if he who is healing is irascible, and if his blood is too acrid and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 then he should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce in vinegar, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 and minced partridge, and roasted meat, and moist food.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And he who has a cold constitution should take syrup of honey, and medium-aged aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and minced pullet, and minced partridge and small birds and thrushes.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and on the day he purges himself, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 and it is necessary to give some men sometimes theriac or mastic before purging, or after, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The blisters that are placed without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the bladder, and for gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hip, because these members cannot be cut on the eyes, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, just as we place them on the breasts when the child nurses;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 to remove the swelling that is in the member, just as we place blisters on the belly and groin to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and removes the pain, when there is an ulcer or stone, and by its attractive power it draws out the ulcer, or moves the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 And so it does when placed on the liver and on the bladder when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty for sucking only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and other times filled with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that the cupping glass is filled solely with hot water or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on its side around the middle a small hole, just large enough to insert a needle, and let it be of brass or soft metal so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And have in the middle a rod of copper or iron crosswise, to place a cloth bandage, and let them be both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And thus must one place this cupping glass upon the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 take the cloth of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping glass across the rod that is inside the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass that it may not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 and then place it upon the member, and your two fingers should be upon the opening that we have mentioned, so that when one wishes, out go the vapors, and remove the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one applies the binding again as before, and often restarts it if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the cupping used for pleurisy, there is no rod or hole in it, and it is only applied when full of water, and is placed on the member alone;
et c’est li forme:	 and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Leeches are only applied in members where one cannot place cupping due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 and in bare flesh places, such as the nostrils or the nose, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 and the quality of the user is that when you find leeches that are in clean, soft waters without impurities, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And he places them in a pot of soft water, until they are familiar with it, and have nothing in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 And then let them be bled from a vein and by cupping, then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply leeches.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and drop off, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, then apply it, for this is very valuable afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, then raise the area with egg whites, and then with water, very well, and then compress it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the area bleeds too much after the leeches, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the bleeding stops.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if the blood is plentiful, apply powdered vitriol, or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is stanched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 or place on the wound half of peeled broad beans, and leave them until they dry up in place, it will now staunch.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the leeches do not want to take [blood], then rub the wound with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry up.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they fall off, then sprinkle on a little powder of aloe and boiled linen, or ash, and they will now fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the setting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Know, dear son, that foolish physicians reject this chapter, for they have never seen any ancient books or letters concerning it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 and for this reason the knowledge has become strange in our land, for I have never found any good one here.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have acquired the knowledge from them, and by experience, and by the practice of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 and I have now described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	 It is necessary therefore that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when a break or dislocation or twist or fracture comes to someone, you must hurry to heal the patient on one side and then the other, unless something prevents it entirely, such as physical weakness, or infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 Or if the season is too hot or too cold.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 And chew on cold foods, that is, cold jellies, and birds and game, and drink no wine, nor chew any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain of no hot abscess or spread of matter in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If the patient returns to his usual diet first.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that promote thickening, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads (of animals), and feet, and cow's pancreas, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For such nourishment, the bone splinters and fractures heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres,
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but do not care, set on the broken bone a strong pin that holds and joins the member together, so that it strengthens as before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not completely take it from its work, and therefore one must feed it with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 And know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	 For there is a fracture that goes across (transverse), and another in oblique direction, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And there is a fracture with wound, and a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And for each type there should be its own device and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes back into place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 and it is known that the bone break occurs because the place is twisted, and opens well from the outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no dislocation or swelling, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it can still have dislocation, a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	 If you do not need to move it with your hand, but rather apply the medicines that follow, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the breaks that go in an arc, and are the two parts dislocated, you must now set them equally, before abscesses form there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses develop there, leave it for some days until the abscesses subside;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 Then set it equally with as little and wise effort as you can, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of one where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 then grasp it, as is required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if there are broken pieces in the bone, then stretch it from two parts, whether it be the hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset all the additions in their places as best you can, and be careful not to cause injury or pain to the patient through your work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 and adjust the two ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If you straighten it beautifully, and do not press too much, nor squeeze like those who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither in wakefulness nor in sleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 and take good care that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when he feels no pain, it is not set properly, and one must put him in such a position that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 and take care that he is placed straightly, so that there will be no twist when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 And the quality of the broken limb is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness, largeness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 and those which are large, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandage embraces all of the large limb, and holds it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 then place around it light stuffing, three or four turns depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little to all the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is moved away slightly.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a great part of the healthy place, then take the other ligament and turn it again around the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 then return to the part below the break and hold it moderately, not too hard nor too soft, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 then place between the ligaments linen or cloth strips, so that they are all even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is swelling or an abscess, place on top something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 then restrain on your shoulders, and let them be of half the width of a strong rope, or of wood from which they make wedges, or of palm fibers, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but it is necessary that the shoulder support placed on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and let it also be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then restrain on the supports in the same way as you did at the first time, then bind over it with a bandage, just as at the first time on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 tighter is above, always less so below;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it is necessary that the bandages be of medium size, not too thick nor too thin, and they should be soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 Because if the threads are thick, just as I have seen the work of fools who make their ligatures from twisted flax cords, and this is a great error, because the ligature cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each knot.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	 And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the stars after the contraction in their healthy places, then place under them linen wicks or shredded wool, so that it does not wound.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	 When the wound is with the fracture, and the heart is broken, I will speak of its treatment later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not necessary to set all the fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 Because when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put in ligatures stronger than after five or seven days, or more according to your surety of heat occurring from an abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 and see here the method of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And it is that you take the flour that stays against the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and put this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fractures in many situations, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Other manner of plaster for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take abreis, ladanum, henbane, asafetida, Arabic gum, and mugwort, amounting to twelve denarii;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 myrrh and aloe, amounting to five denarii;
alechil VIIII З.;	 garlic, nine denarii;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 and make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the man's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another manner of plaster for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take mugwort and marshmallow, amounting to ten denarii;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Mirror and aloe, seven nine.
acaice VI З.;	 Alum, six.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Bole armoricain ten, and grind well, and infuse with plenty of egg water, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another way to make a plaster for displaced joints and dislocated bones, which relieves the resulting pain and uses the bone shards:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the spot.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This poultice does not restore [the joint or bone], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and properly relieves pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another way to make a plaster that mends broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and common dandelion leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of making a poultice for the restoration of bone fractures and to draw out the remaining pus from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of marsh mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, one part each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind, and cook with wine, and if the limb is heated, cook with moist coriander water or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of poultice stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of marsh mallow, and flax seed, mallow, melilot, and comfrey, and violet flowers and chamomile, one part each;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 and grind, and cook with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Ypocras says in his book that nothing should be put on a broken limb to restore its strength except for a cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and it should be between two [things], not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems to Galen that dry and slightly warm things should be put on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another plaster recipe that is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take mullein and chopped onions, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and celery equally, and crush them, and make a poultice with it and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 Then unbind it after a while, and see if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone has moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 then do not unbind for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain comes to the place, or itching without rest or swelling, then hurry and unbind it, and remove the poultice immediately;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 and take a light cloth, and a wet sponge of sea water, and dip it in water, and lift the place until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a knot, until you are sure of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 and the inflammation of the limb will subside, and the pain will be gone, then begin with a subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and continue with this until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, I have removed everything from it, and you need plaster and linen, then start again, just as you did first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing happens to the limb as we have said, do not unbind it until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break heals, and the skin approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then restrain him more than before, and it increases his flesh.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 And if you see the place drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Therefore, apply hot water dressing each time you loosen him, every three days, and slightly loosen the bandage.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 Through this work, nourishment is brought to the limb and quickly improves what foolish physicians do, who wrongly return the twisted limb.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 This is bad, and it is a dangerous practice, and I see nothing else to do but to let it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 Of the various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 Many kinds of fractures are there, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 for there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the neck removes all the bone up to the marrow which is beneath the bone, like an axe or a stake;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 When the sword strikes the bone from above without penetrating it, this manner of fracture is called "absolue";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	 And if there is a blunt force trauma, or a splinter or a kick from a stone, or from falling onto stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 And if there is a deep cut that reaches the tissue beneath the bone or on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And there is a wound that is filled in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 and there is the wound that is made by striking with a stone or falling or something similar, which causes a piece of bone to enter lower, and the place is indented like when blacksmiths strike on the anvils;
si entre li piere dedens.	 if between the stones within
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it occurs with all these types of fracture where small fragments are separated like stars.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 Et reconnaître toutes les manières de fractures par la traction sur elles, et l'interrogatoire avec des sondes, et par la chair corrompue qui est dessus.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 The similarity to hair is known by this: when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the care of the fracture, beware of the patient's accidents, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of senses, stretching, paleness, fever, and others in many dispositions, then he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded person comes to you first, and this is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the new moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the flesh under the bone becomes corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, you must split the split part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as gently as possible. And if blood flows when uncovering the bone or an abscess like this, let him be helped with what is necessary. And it is that you fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be assured of no further bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 one way is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then he puts in another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second way is that you have various cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are of steel;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And work lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must bore through it before you administer cuts with trepans, not so deep that they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; xspace
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 and you must have several of them, so that each comes in its place on the bone's width, so that you have splints for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and it is in the form of three kinds of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one splint on the bone and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then place the splint elsewhere a little while after, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand or any of the instruments you have such as pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And make sure you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you then use the instrument that remains attached to the bone for all other similar instruments resembling a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if there remains anything of the small bones or any scales, then gently remove them with an instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 Then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And the other method of work is that which Galen says is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and he praises it greatly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, where the fracture is open, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place under the head of this lancet-like instrument, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut on one side, and the part is bent in two sides, so that the cutting tool is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly tap around the entire bone, and be careful of the cloth underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 if it is rough against the bone, then lightly smooth it out, for one can remove it well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 Et si la fracture de l'os ne perce pas jusqu'à la peau, et que l'os est coupé seulement par le dessus, avec des petits morceaux, alors il faut gratter cette aspérité et retirer les écailles à l'aide d'un rasoir subtil, dont tu dois avoir différentes quantités pour administrer dans chaque endroit ce qui est le plus approprié, selon la nature du travail et la forme de la fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	 Et si l'os présente des fissures profondes, utilise d'abord un grand rasoir, puis un rasoir plus fin, et continue ainsi jusqu'à ce qu'il soit bien poli.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other subtle cuts and breaks, you must bring the cause according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 and this is something that has not been answered by one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is exposed, then you must take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 then take another doublet, folded in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first doublet;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the surface, then place another ligature on top, and do not tighten it any stronger than necessary to touch the wound only;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is appeased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 and of these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer medicines modestly without harshness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And see to it that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any ointment in it, and do not let pus gather, because when pus gathers on the caul of the brain, it will run and putrefy, and great evil befalls the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 for when one applies to the wound a biting thing, it necrotizes on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Take care therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness comes to it except for the medicine that one has applied, which has such power, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and make a plaster with them, and apply it to the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then continue the care in various ways as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 You should know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, either one alone or both together, for these are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And that below is made of gristle and does not break, but only causes a swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or a probe into the nose, and equalize that fracture within your middle finger, and hold it in place by force until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 Do this gently, and be careful not to cause the patient pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	 And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach it, then you must place it evenly at the end of a thick reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 And if the fracture is of both parts, then do the same, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 se ce non, after the seventh or tenth day, when this abscess is healed, then apply to the head of the nose bandages of linen cloths, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 Or you place another [bandage] on the other side, if the fracture is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 And let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some say that one must grease the threads in butter and change them daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem to me that this is good, but they must be moistened in the making of a mixture of egg and flour.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Then leave the bandage until the bones are healed and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes one places goose feathers in the nose instead of bandages, and then wraps a soft cloth around it, and if the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through it.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 And do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if such an abscess comes to the nose while you work there, place a poultice of cotton soaked in rose oil or a little bit of aquiline.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if such abscesses do not form, then apply an external plaster made of sesame flour and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then place light dressings on top, and do not bind the neck.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 And if the neck fracture is small and broken into many pieces, then reset it with suitable instruments, then sew up the gap, and treat similar flesh wounds, and let them heal, such as suitable plasters and bandages for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no wound inside the neck, then treat it with tents, and place lead weights in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	 Of the jawbone dislocation
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jawbone is dislocated beneath, and there is no wound outside of it, and the fracture is only outside, and it is not broken in two, except for being indented inside, then one recognizes it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then insert your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inside, and fix it with the other hand from outside, and align it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	 And if the jawbone fracture is divided into two, then you must administer traction on both parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if there is movement or dislocation of the teeth, then fasten them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place wax on the broken jaw, and put on a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 and place on the cloth a large, well-made splint, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above the teeth as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat only light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the appearance changes, then dislocate it on the third day, and then reset at the place where it changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 And apply a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the wax;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And put on a light cloth over the plaster, and if the plaster dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is cured.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 often he is cured in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 And if an abscess like this occurs, bring it about as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, inspect whether any piece of bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 then remove it with the appropriate instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound if it is wide, and place on it suitable plasters to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	 of the splint
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The ligament breaks several times in front of, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three types:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 where it is broken and separated into two parts, and there are fragments, and this is the easiest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 or there is fracture with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the work of this is when the fracture is without wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the ligament is broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other extends the neck towards the side.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 then place the fracture evenly between your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no deviation or swelling. xspace
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend more, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity. xspace
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And stretch and raise the bandage, and press the sphere to your hand, so that you set the break evenly as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the bone out due to its depth, it is necessary that the patient lie on their back, and place under the shoulder a pillow of medium size, and the assistant presses the shoulder down until the bones of the broken limb are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 And then adjust the break with your fingers, and if you find it splintered, it is necessary to split open.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 And draw out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, then cut it with one of the incisors that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 But place this instrument under the bandage to protect the flesh.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 And it looks like a spoon, and is not curved, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work. ething look
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 And it should have two points, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound you made when you drew out the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are certain of a hot abscess, stitch the wound, and if the rupture is small or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if such abscesses occur, soak the cloth in rose oil and basil and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds or cuts, is to place on the bone a plaster made from mill powder and egg white, then put light wadding on top, and place a splint underneath if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then put a double cloth on top of the wadding and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a thin strip of three fingers' width and length, and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the star above the break, and turn the bandage around the neck, and beneath the healthy shoulder, and beneath the sick shoulder.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And reset each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break well, and you see clearly that the star does not move above the broken bone, then bandage it every day, and when the ligature loosens, then bind it again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the healthy shoulder while they sleep, to raise the sick shoulder.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 Thus the fracture will be relieved of its heaviness by the elevation of the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an accident occurs, for up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then renew the poultice, if you see that it is necessary, and hold it and leave it thus, until it is healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And it is healed in as many as 28 days, or less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	 of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks in a large place or in the middle, and it is not known except by touching;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 If you prepare it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 Then put on the place powder of mill with plenty of egg, and light stuffing, and put on a double cloth;  ()
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 Then put on a wide and fine bandage, somewhat wider than the shoulder, and if there is an indentation in any part of the shoulder under the bandage, fill that hollow with flax stuffing so that the bandage lies evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 And then he binds it firmly with a large bandage so that the joint does not move from its place, and checks the ligature every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And every time it loosens, he binds it again and sets the joint straight if it is out of place, and the patient lies on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 And the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is completed, he unbinds it, and be assured, for it is not an easy thing to displace the bone.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a fragment of the bone protrudes forward and pierces beneath the heart, it rises up and removes the bone, and does as we have said in the breaking of the rib to heal an abscess, hot.
de la brisure dou pis	 of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 But it often breaks at the toe.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in half, it inclines downward and the patient feels great pain, and fainting, and dizziness, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the wound in the broken bone, which can be felt well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back, and he places a pillow between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and joins the ribs from the second rib with both hands, and does his best to straighten it in all ways possible until the bone's shape is as it should be; abei
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 then place plasters and wool over the thin layer of salt, or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and secure it over the broken bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 and turn the bandage around the back, and fasten it firmly, and check every hour the binding, and if it becomes loose, then tighten it.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to loosen it, due to inflammation or itching that occurs in the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and apply whatever has come of the various treatments.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then replace the plaster, and fasten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Saiches that the breaking of ribs occurs only in large bones behind the back, and inside the head, and they break only because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 And the patient feels it well during questioning, just as they should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is that you set the fracture evenly, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a plaster and bind it with a bandage, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the breaking of the ribs is slanting inwards, then the patient feels very great pain and sharpness, as if from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And breathes with difficulty and coughs up great plants of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients had great ingenuity in it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And so there are those who say that he should be given food that bloats the stomach to push out the break.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	 We do not do this, for hot abscesses may come if they are not already present.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And some say that one should place cupping glasses on the spot to draw out greatly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 If fear arises that the cupping might draw the excesses to the place due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some say that the site should be covered with wool soaked in hot oil, and tents should be placed between the ribs to make the lung even all around, then let it be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone that pierces the flesh, and there is fear in the patient, then one must cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the hypochondrium.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then one should cut the bone and gently pull it out, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 And if these abscesses come, then place wet cloths in rose oil on the spot;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat it as you would an abscess, and let it lie on its back on the side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	 of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it may bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And so too with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note whether you see his hands becoming soft and swollen and numb, and he cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that he is mortal in many cases, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pulled and pricked, know that the bone's joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if he is treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 And if something similar happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it is healed or not, take care whether the feet are weakened, and if there are accidents that are in the hands, and on the back is a swelling and evacuation without control;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And when it has been placed on its belly, there is an evacuation without control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is healed on its back and it wants to rise, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 Know that it is fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 If he does not work hard at his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if this does not happen to him, then the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is such that if there is a hot abscess, you should place hot rose oil or egg yolk oil on it until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
