Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 And if any bone is dislocated, you must cover it with the curette.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And remove the bone, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches if it is large, and treat it with incisional healing ointment until healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," insert your thumb from your left hand and align it with the other hand to your power, then place the poultice and bandage on top, if you need to.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Then hold it firmly in place, and if there are any bone fragments, bring them out, remove them, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	 Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It happens sometimes that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, it has no more strength than a little weakening at the top;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 And the leg becomes long, and leans to one side, and the patient feels pain in that place, and sharpness, and swells like it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 And the reduction is such that you extend your hand upwards until you are above the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and know what the fracture and its shape are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 and if the fracture is only at the end, set it straight until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	 And if the break is lengthwise, or tilts inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until you are prepared to restore this break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have set it straight, apply a poultice, then place a splint of wood or bone on top, and secure the fracture so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 and bind the area below the ribs until the limb is straight.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	 Command the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and then apply what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 And then return to the resetting, and hold it as needed if there is no bad incident.
et c’est li maniere.	 And that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The shoulder is what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be reset according to one of the two methods.
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 one method is that you take a stick full of medium thickness, like this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And tie it to the two heads with two ties, and pull upwards, and have the patient sit on a chair.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 then have the patient throw his broken arm onto the stick until it reaches the armpit, and have in the middle of the stick an arch of wood, then pull up with some heavy object or the assistant extends downward.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then let the physician place the splint equal to his hands together, so that the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And the other method is that one places the patient on his back, and ties the hand to his neck; then commands two assistants: one to hold what is above the fracture in his hands, and the other to hold below all the joint, and each stretches at his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tighten each ligament below the break and above the break, and extend each of the members to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the splint is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you place one strap in the middle under the arm, and another towards the elbow, under the splint;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 and also if the splint is towards the elbow, it is necessary to place a strap lightly, without effort, so that the splint is equal on the place, and on the elbow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 then make the splint even, as it should be, and bind it, if there are no abscesses there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses come there, do not bind until the seventh day, and place moist linen on it in ease and rose oil, so that these abscesses may be appeased;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 then it is restrained, and the manner of restraining it is that you place the compress on the break, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 and place the bandage, and restrain on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in the position of a star, if nothing hinders it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone will move, use of stars is required. Place on the break a star wider and stronger than the others, and there should be two fingers' width between each star, and each star should be so large that it passes beyond the break by three fingers on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then pull up on the shoulders as I said at the beginning of the chapter on breaking bones, more strongly and less in stretching.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the setting of the shoulders and the pulling as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it to be bound for seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then check every three days the bandage, that no itching or swelling comes to the place, where the care cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you receive it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such incident happens, then do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 And place under the shoulder a pillow filled with wool equally, and observe every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken member does not move, or be softened the ligament;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 if he receives it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously described, in such a way that the food is first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 and when he begins to recover, let it be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be taken for forty days in total;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 and then one must free him and administer a bath and remedies of ointments to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and clogged, it will take days or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm's fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two scapulae", one of which is small and follows the shoulder blade;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the other is large, and it is the one below, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 perhaps the large phalanx breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small phalanx is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then you should extend it slightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 And if it is the large phalanx, then it must be held more tightly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 and extend it on a cushion, and hold the patient's hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no discomfort; ︎
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then let the minister extend his arm to the lower part under his hand, or at one ligament, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then let the physician set it straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the fracture is in pieces, then put each one in its place; and if there is any that sticks out which you cannot restore to its place, then cut it off and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And if there is a fracture with a wound, I have spoken about it in a separate chapter.
si pren la cure.	 If he takes the care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 And if in the beginning of the treatment there are such abscesses, then attach a piece of plaster made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And delicately place the cloth on top, until these abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 And then remove the plaster, and apply a poultice of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then apply the bandages, and let the bandage of the fracture be always stronger, and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that there must be six stars on the arm in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 and apply more pressure on the break than elsewhere, and always less while stretching, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 and let the bandages that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And return the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 And if some evil accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must wash the limb with hot water until that itch is appeased.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And let the limb not rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the splinting again, and if the ligament is softened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, set it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you take care that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, then you should soften it in a poultice and leave it like this for some days until the nourishment reaches there, and then splint it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 Et si aucune de ces choses que nous avons dites ne vient au malade, alors ne le délier pas avant vingt jours.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 or, in which case, let him place his hands on his neck, and his shoulders should be even, and he should guard against movement and shifting, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And know that this fracture is healed in thirty days or thirty-five, and sometimes in twenty days, according to the composition and complexion of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	 De la fracture de la main
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Sachez que dans le dos de la main et aux jointures des doigts il arrive peu de fractures, et qu'il ne s'y produit que des entorses à plusieurs reprises.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged, and sits upright in front of him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 then let him place his hand on the stretched cloth, and let the attendant straighten the broken bones, and let the physician set them evenly until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And place the plaster and bandages, if no abscess occurs, then place a needle according to the size of the place.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 And if the break is on the side around the waist of the leg, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken leg.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And then bind it with a long cloth, and let the needle be as soft as a human hair, and as large as the palm of the hand, and tie it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the fracture is at the tip, it is necessary that you place a splint on top and another below at the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie all around the hand, and secure the bandage between the two fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 And if the break is in any of our fingers, if it is protruding, set it straight as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 And hold it with the sole, and if you see thus place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the fracture is in one of the other fingers, such as the index or any other, set it straight, and tie it with the sound finger that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Or you bind them all together in one bandage, as needed, or you place a splint on top, like a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And take care in the restoration and placement of a hot abscess, and support whoever comes to help, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The thigh bone is often broken, and it is well seen when it twists forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And the restoration is such that one ligament is tied above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 And the patient lies on his back, then each minister extends his line equally to his part.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 and this is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ties should be towards the knee, and the other tie below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 And so if it is near the knee, then let the line be below the knee, and the extension downwards.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 then let the surgeon put the bone equal with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the dressing, and bind it, if no abscess comes there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to settle, then return to your work and care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 You must wrap over the fracture one bandage double-layered in two or three places, leaving excess material. Then turn the leg until the heel comes to the base of the nail, and thread a long string between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, making the ends meet above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put on the break splints, and place a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to make the splint even, then begin to tie tightly three or four times on the break;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 and when you go higher up the break, tie it less tightly.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 then attach at two ends of the thread that you have passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are on top, then go back down to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 and secure it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, for if there is no abscess or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and address whatever comes of it, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 And if there are bone fragments that prick, they must be removed, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 And if it is not possible, then the place should be split open and pulled out strongly.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 And sometimes the thigh bone breaks like splinters, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 nonetheless, in such a restoration the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days, or a little less or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 of the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the tendon of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a fissure or a hole, and this happens in every wound, both in open and closed wounds, and everyone feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And the restoration is such that one should place equal what is broken on each side, so that it is assembled as well as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 Then apply the poultice, and if you need it, place a round spindle in it, and bind it as required. Then follow all the instructions we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses or similar ones;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If he applies to each injury what is necessary until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is rightly called "tibia," and the other is called "fibula.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 And all other fractures happen as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the workings are the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg twists in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 Et s'il y a une fracture d'un grand os, on ressent une grande douleur, et cela est visible.
et torne desoz.	 et cela se retourne en dessous.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Alors, appliquez une traction pour l'aligner, et fixez les éclisses de manière égale;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 Cependant, si la fracture est complexe avec plusieurs fragments, il faut appliquer une traction plus douce et légère;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Et alignez-le selon vos compétences.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 Et lorsque vous avez terminé votre travail, prenez deux bandes de bois tournées qui enveloppent la jambe de chaque côté, et qu'elles soient aussi longues que la jambe du genou jusqu'en bas;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 then wrap in two places with one bandage on top and one below, and tie it in the middle as well. In this manner, the leg will not be able to bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 and some place a stick along the length of the leg, which is made of wood, and they put the leg in to prevent movement. Properly, this is done in a fracture where there is an injury;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 and each day they move the leg to see if there is an abscess or any other incident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 if the treatment continues until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no fracture, but sometimes the foot bones break and the two bones, and in this case, it happens more often as a shattering in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones surpassing one another, then place the sick person's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and now put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 Then put the poultice and wool on top, and place under the foot a small table with two full feet, then bind the foot tightly, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, then dislocate the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if there are any of the two broken, then restore them, as we have said for the hands;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot that small table I mentioned, and bind it tightly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the table under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And let it stand on top of the head of the table away from the stomach of the foot, so that it grasps well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have spoken of before;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 and treat each case as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the bone of a woman's natural birth is broken, let her sit widened, then incline it towards the back, and hold it from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 then fill the woman's natural birth cavity with cotton, and put as much in as is necessary.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 then make the woman stand up and raise her back little by little, and thus the cotton will come out until it reaches the entrance of the birth, and the bone will return with the cotton. 
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton; when she has finished, replace it, and do this for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 then the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a cord to its opening, and insert it entirely into the vulva.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 then blow strongly into the cord until the bladder is inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 thus the fracture will return to its natural position.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the bone of a man's or woman's wrist is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the hip bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And these fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and practice into it, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For the fracture indicates in many cases the right way for restoration
enten le donques.	 Therefore, understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put the penis in it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone who has a breaking with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cauterized immediately, so that the cauteries that we have mentioned prove it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else; then begin again to restore the break in that same hour, or that day, if no abscess forms there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if an abscess forms there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed; and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause evil to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding from the surface of the skin, then you must handle it lightly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the extension is not ready to be put equally in your hands, then use this iron instrument which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 and therefore it is necessary for the doctor to prepare three or four, according to how many he will need for each fracture treatment;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palanche," for which reason the curved head should be placed on top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 and strike it once, so that it returns, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then strike it with a suitable instrument for this purpose, either an incision tool or a saw, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 then remove that which remains in the bone by scraping and fine shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 If it is so that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stringent wine, and carefully if it is in summer.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 And do not put any greasy ointment or other oil on the wound, lest it brings about putrefaction and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 Then administer steel when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the dressing all around it, according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not constricted with the splint.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And many times have foolish doctors done this, causing either death or corruption in the patient.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 And let the splint be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 Et si la plaie est grande ou mauvaise, et tu crains qu'un accident ne survienne, comme nous l'avons dit, et tu trouves de la douleur à cet endroit, alors il ne faut pas appliquer d'étoupes;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 mais envoloupe autour de la plaie, au lieu d'étoupes, des linges durs, et les attache.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two that the swelling begins to grow on the wound, then remove everything you have put on in all haste, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetracycline ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bone descends lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot be joined together but the bone returns again, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must explore the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an ulcer comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 Et quant l'os est cassé et perce à travers le membre, comme l'os de la cuisse ou de l'épaule, ainsi que d'autres grands membres similaires, ne le retire pas, car souvent cela entraîne la mort. Mais laisse-le en place jusqu'à ce qu'il pourrisse;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 par aventure il tombera de lui-même après vingt jours ou trente, puis soigne la plaie, si tu le peux;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 over bruises that come onto the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 We often find ourselves after the health of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is bad to see;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 and by chance the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Take care then if the bone is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 if you administer astringent medicines to him, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and cook them with stiptic wine or plenty of egg or honey; 》
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 and place them on the wound in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 And then it dislocates again, and starts another, until the dislocation is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 Or you stretch it over a well-made piece of wood;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 Because the property of wood is that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 And if the dislocation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then scrape over it, and make the excess visible;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Or you shave it with a scraper until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the fracture of the bone is set, but afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 One reason is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 Or because there were too many ligaments, and nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 or due to excessive bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 or due to excessive movement, not at its proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 or because he has little blood in his body, he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and soften the body until the blood increases in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 and administer baths to him, and give him joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment to it, and frequently wash it with warm water until the nourishment reaches the limb; ние
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 About the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is visible, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb again entirely, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 and these actions are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 nevertheless, if the swelling and the pain are recent, it is necessary that they be bathed in hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of plantain, roots, and marshmallow, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 and make a softening plaster, as well-made Diasculon, and you take the mucilage of plantain, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When you take fat figs, grind them with colon seed, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continuously and vigorously rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement applied to the member each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 And if the hardness and rigidity are like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with an iron instrument, then you must cut it down to the bone gently with a fine incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 and put poultices and plasters on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation is the displacement of a joint from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation occurs in someone, they must be brought back to sense immediately. ‌
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 For if one delays, then the place swells, and perhaps it is hardly put back in place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 therefore it should not be moved at the time when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 many times it brings on spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 however, when this happens, make the patient sweat, then leave him until the abscess subsides;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Then bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have arranged the chapters of the dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 It often happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two methods.
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 either they are slightly removed from their places, and softened a little
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the patient drools from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and the tongue is wrapped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in many ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 And if it is complete and full, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the doctor puts a little finger of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 And let the other two fingers of the hands be lacking, to make it equal.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And instruct the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the doctor should set it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 And if the jaw is swollen, even if it is both jaws together, then rinse them with hot water and oil until they are lightly reset.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 Do not delay in treating the swelling, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are equally reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without slackening, then place moistened cloths on top, made with rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 And let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two pillows, so that they do not move it to the right or left, nor should they try to chew, but take only light food until the pain is relieved and the jaws are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And then he chews what he wants lightly, and does not labor to open his mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well knitted and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set right within an hour and are not restored to their proper places, fever and abscesses follow, and perhaps a ruptured bowel, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times he who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 from the armpit
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The armpit cannot dislocate from the inside of the body or from the hip, and sometimes it is dislocated by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 and then presses the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 then apply the plaster and bindings, and tighten them;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 and the head which is towards the knife cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 if it does not, and if it ever dislocates again, reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then apply the plaster and bind it, and hold it steady, and instruct the patient to rest until healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And in the same way is reduced the head of the shoulder when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Know that the shoulder is only dislocated according to three methods:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 one of which is when it dislocates down towards the lower part of the armpit;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 and the second is towards the side of the chest;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 and sometimes it dislocates upwards, which happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 and it does not dislocate backwards due to the shoulder, nor inwards due to the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for with them it jumps up quickly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 at those who have enough flesh, though it is barely so, and enters with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And sometimes it happens to some men due to injury or breakage, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Therefore, you must test it until you are certain about it.
et adonques encomence la cure.	 And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 The dislocation is known when it descends towards the shoulder blade and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear diversity between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 And you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and under the shoulder blade, at the back, the head of the shoulder as if it were an egg.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 And the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor can he make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 Similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly at the back.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And this manner of dislocation is not easy to reset when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 And the manner is that the caregiver lifts the hand of the patient up, then places their fingers underneath the arm, and lifts the joint with force up to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 And the caregiver lifts the hand, and extends it upward, then places it underneath;
si venra hastanment.	 so that it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 And if it does not come as we have said in a few days afterwards, then the patient must be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 and the caregiver should gently soften and soothe it, as with a decoction of hops and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 Then let the patient lie on his back, and place under the buttocks a pad of cloth, neither too soft nor too hard. Then the physician places his heel on the pad, lifts the head of the shoulder skillfully, and pulls the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 and another assistant holds the patient's head so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see this, you should reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 and it is necessary for there to be a man present who is larger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 and he should stand next to the patient's side, and push his shoulder under the patient's buttocks, and lift the buttocks up high, so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And another minister draws the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, then some heavy object should be placed with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 And one resets it in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 and it is as if one drives a long log into the ground, so that the head is as round as a fist, neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft cloths on top, and the patient should be standing alongside the log;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 then his hand should be stretched down strongly from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 take a log of two feet in length and four inches in width, which has the head round to easily enter deeply under the saddle, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 Then lay it on the patient's head under a cloth so that the stick does not hurt the patient, then place it under the patient's pillow.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 And extend one arm along the length of the stick, and place the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the top of the hand, then place the arm on the rung of a ladder, and let the hand hang down, and let the body hang from the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 The joint will return to its proper place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is in place, whichever way it may be, you must put underneath the seat an equal sphere of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with mill powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it. Then fasten it securely under the seat, and turn the ligature over the plaster, and encircle the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 And he should move it little by little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 and then move it more after five or seven days, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And if it is immobile and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the juncture is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauteries to three places, as is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm above, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 The dislocations that are towards the foot and ankles, or behind, are done by pushing and stretching with the hands, and another ligament is administered there.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and care for it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after the healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, then let the patient take many baths until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the shoulder joint is easily dislocated and easily returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 and it can be dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not hidden, because one can see it well and feel it well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 And it dislocates according to each joint.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick member with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm, nor can he touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 And you must reset it before any abscesses form there, because if abscesses were to form, it would be difficult to restore.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is in the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 it is worse than other dislocations, and it causes more pain, and perhaps death will occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And the restoration is such that when it is in a position where it can be reset, you should extend its hand with both of your hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and the arm should be spread out, and place your hands according to the length around, above and below, and press the joint together, at its base or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is forward, then it returns when he folds his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the knife that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer a strong extension.
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 and when the master joins the joint with his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 and when it is in place, then apply a dry plaster with some egg white, and press firmly, and bandage the arm around the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then unbandage it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is firmly in place, unbind the ligament, and let it go;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 and if you see that the joint does not stretch well, then restart the bandage and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	 then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if after the joint is reset he feels tightness and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 or you put a greasy sheepskin over the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the sheepskin back on, and then enter the bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this two or three times, until it is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 and if you see (this), then place moist, warm cow dung with butter on top, and bind it up;
si revenra a sa disposition.	 it will return to its proper place.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the relocation is light, more than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 However, it must be returned to its place immediately, in the same hour that it is dislocated, before the place becomes swollen, or a hot abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the relocation is done by placing the diseased hand on a table, and the assistant extends his hand, and the doctor places his hand in line with it, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 Nevertheless, you must check if it is in place.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then have the patient lay their back on a table for extension and flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then let the patient place the back of their hand on a table, and let the physician place his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, that's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, then apply soothing plasters for abscesses like these, and leave it alone without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains misaligned.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 And this does not harm the patient any more than while the hand is wet, and cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 Then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 If there is no other means than to restrain by fire cautery near the case, and perhaps it does not matter otherwise.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then moisten it with hot water and rub until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the wrist.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 then extend the finger, and push the dislocation towards your pockets until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 and leave it for two days, and then put it back in place on the third day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 and bind it tightly as we have said, and unbind it each day, and make it move, and rebind it tight.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and do this often, until it is healed, and do the same if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, and proceed as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do likewise when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 And the signs are that the excretion jumps out without wanting to, and cannot be held, and often some members are softened, whether both thighs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And often the spine moves in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 that which moves to the back is called "scoliosis":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 the remedy for this is to reduce it if the scoliosis has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 then there is no remedy or healing for it all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancients speak of remedies in grand words, where there is not always great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 But I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the jaundice that affects the breast first, there is no sense or health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 and so it is with jaundice that comes directly to the two sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes specifically to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 and let the patient be laid on his side in an equal place, and have support beneath him, so that he does not injure himself;
